O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is behind the science of medicine, having accomplished it, through his explanations and by his declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it was given to me in vision that I would complete this treatise with this work, which is part of the book of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the book of hands is distorted in our region and is strange throughout, so that it is lost knowledge and forgotten, and there remains from them only a few small descriptions in books of the ancients who had moved their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arose errors and vanities, and the intentions were closed, and the knowledge was withdrawn.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I can revive her by observing the order of this treatment according to the way of exposure and declaration and abridgment;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I will assemble the forms of the cautery tools and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation for them, just as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is fitting for one who enters into this that to surpass in anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the joint of the limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and marrow and the number of joints, and the departure and movement of the veins, and their rest, and so that he know the source from which they issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And because Hippocrates said that the knife with the blunt edge is much better, and with the work it's poor;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and in the art of hand itself.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	Let us say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not aware of what has been said, will be careful to avoid making an error and not offend others;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	After that I've had to endure many more of those who contradict this knowledge, and abandon it in favor of their own ignorance and foolishness.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	But I saw a madman who cut the apostoem of scrofuls or the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries at the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	and for this reason, so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another madman who treated a stone from an old man's foot, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took out a piece of the bladder with it, and died within three days of his illness.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen that this is called for the treatment, and I see the state of the patient and the size of the wound, and I know well whether the patient will die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another madman who took in the treatment of a duke of our land who had broken his leg, and with the breakage got wounds;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the mismanaged plain of ignorance holds back the breach on the wound with great force, and does not allow it to heal at all, and leaves it so that I will finish.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and instruct him not to touch it again;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and held back so that the leg was completely exposed and the feet came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am summoned to come to him, but I delayed coming to release the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I saw it dislocated he was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the corruption had already been confirmed in that limb, and it could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And do not stop the corruption of the limb until all the limbs have perished.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there are other signs that can cause an abscess to form and then inflame, due to the malice of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humors, does not suit to touch it with iron unless there is some relief so that one can remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	which is to say, how it has perils in various conditions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each one of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	So that you will keep it safe, so that the foolish might not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your arms in consideration, and undertake your patients lightly but firmly, and use the best way, so that through God's grace you come to safety and are praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	Let loose the fearful diseases of the body's health.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And take back your arms from that which makes you doubt, and hold fast in them so that you may come to this world from the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	The Galen's writings say in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Don't take treatment for a bad disease unless you are called mad.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are of fire cautery and of cauterization with aqua medicina, and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of forms of discharges, and of cauterization instruments, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and wounds, and extractions of arrows, and similar things.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and are the chapters arranged and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twisting, and similar things.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is arranged with the size of each instrument just as with pieces, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Also that we remember the work, it is fitting to say which quality of aid and how much pain each condition causes.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help and of harm are the longest word and subtle science and the secrets of response.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and this is what many wise men spoke about, and agreed upon;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and let them spare him from my words, for I have a great longing.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cauterization helps universally with all kinds of matter, whether it is flesh or skin.
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that I mean, hot complexion by matter and dry complexion by matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry mixture of matter, some have investigated and said that cauterization is great aid.
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cauterization is of no help to disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured by heat when it is from dryness, nor from cold.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and it is said by those who speak against cautery that it provides great aid to diseases hot and dry, which come into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you buy the body of a man and its moisture is in the condition of fire, you find the body frozen.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And all veins, do not enter fire except for those who have tested it, and who know by long use of the cautery scalpel, and the diversity of human complexion, and the disposition and the causes of their diseases, and remedies, and the space required for each.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	For other complexion types we have little fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians agree with it.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that cutting is a fire composed of cures, and has greater benefit than burning with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire cautery, it is simple, and does not come from fire to other limbs except when applied to the limb that is burned, and does no harm to another limb if its name is known.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Medicines that come from one part of the body to another by separating, and bring illness and pain to the healthy parts.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And in case it stops the sick person.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire does not do this for its height and for the gentleness of its substance; if it has a surplus.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experimentation and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and this is in the words of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And for this reason I excuse the length of my words, because it does not please me to take away from you the secret that is revealed by fire, and the quality of the work, as to how it cures diseases of the body, just as the philosopher says in demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Or (it) is received in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agree on when the cauteries should be made, and take oaths.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cauterization is effective in all times, because the enduring evils are overcome by the aid of cauterization;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and himself, when the cautery is done, for necessary pains and suffering that cannot wait until greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think at all, dear boy, if how a foolish man falls.
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	because the disease which is cured by cautery has no return.
et il le dient ensi;	and he says so;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it's not so as they think, because cautery is not just a medicine that moves the complexion, and dries out the humors which are the cause of pain, but it's valued less than medicine for its haste, and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And another thing is that disease may arise at any time according to the complexion of the sick person and the nature of the disease and its virtue.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And the superfluities are assembled in him through the acquisition of meat and similar things, unless you administer cauterization to him when he has little superfluity and moisture, just as cauteries for dens for pain, and similar things, because no more pain returns.
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens little by little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many do not understand why cauterization is called the "back" of medicine, because it's seen.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is cauterization the "back" of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in no disease and they are useless, then we must administer to them the cauterization, and it is valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And then open the fire cautery carefully, because it is on the back of medicine, not contrary to the understanding of the mad doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient people said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more effective than one made of iron, and they did not say that fires were used only for the quality of gold and because of its high substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	And they said that the wounds from cautery do not cause decay, but it is not truly so because I have proven it, and have found that it happens in some people;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Cautery with gold is more valuable than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And you do not know when you heat an instrument of gold, whether it has cooled down because of the color of the gold, and if so.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if you heat it too much;
si font au feu;	If they prick at their base;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus it is a sufficient hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have tried many times on our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or we have ordered this chapter of the lower limbs to be written first because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	for the olive oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and in it there are two remedies: one made because of a disease called 'soda', and another because of many humors that come out from the head to the eyes, ears, and nose, and for many headaches and pain in the teeth and throat, and likewise for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by medicinal solution to cleanse and clarify the head or three parts, as each virtue and medicine and the custom of the sick can endure.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then put back the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit, cross one leg over the other with your hands, and put his hands on either side of him.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	Then place the root of your palm above the root of his nose between his two eyes.
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and where your two fingers meet, if it bleeds then exhale the cautery called "olive", because of this it is.
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And put the signet of the seal on the left shoulder; and do this by descending and extracting your hand a little at a time while turning it around.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then lift your hand insensibly, and reward the left shoulder if you see a small bone.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After taking a little rest, and applying a poultice made of wool and moist cotton within, put it on the shoulder, and let it be for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After putting a wet cloth in butter on top.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it be until the scab is fallen off.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a treatment for the wound of the tendon, which is called "tetrafarmacoñ", so long as it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients say that when the wound remains open for a longer time, it becomes purged.
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore use ointments.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must cut the cautery so much that a part of the bone is burned, and then replace what was burned with the bone, and then be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And the others say that one should cut the wound so much the longer it is exposed, and pound it so hard as you press down on the bone just as wide as a spindle used by women for sewing because this causes the humors to come out loose.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must expose the wound for a longer time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	After that, one must cure and soothe.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two kinds of cauterizations do not seem to me to be good for everything, fire that in some men has a voice of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I think I should leave it.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the joints are weakened by continuous exposure to natural remedies, as we have seen in other parts of the body.
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and myself consider that the joints of a patient are weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more salutary and healing for me, therefore I make use of this method accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in all the head comes chronic pain that lasts for a long time, then the patient must use the "cough" medicine and pills called so, and purgatives of the head, ointments, and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if you make the fire cautery as we have previously described, and it is worthless.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Be careful that if the head of the sick person is of great strength and not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	and therefore apply the cautery below that which we have previously described above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After making the fire cautery on each corner of the head just above the bone, as we have previously described, and make the cautery on the part called "vassez";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is this where one puts vases;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and hold your hand so that you do not see the bone;
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is fitting that the fire cauterys of the horns are more subtle than those of the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in the middle of the head there is sudden pain and the illness is extended up to the joint, and the joints are purged with medicines made from onions, and other treatments have been done as I have said in the division of diseases, and none of these things help.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	and therefore the fire cautery is done in two ways, that is to say with sharp medicine and with heat.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery with sharp medicine is that you prick with a small needle and remove the skin and then expose two joints, and then make an incision on the temple where the pain holds in this manner so that you can replace the small needle underneath the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it is reset, if the limb and its joint are properly set and left for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then loosen the limb and apply fire to the wound, leaving it so for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put a cloth soaked in butter over the wound so that the infection may cease.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After treatment with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see so, do as I have written or ordered for treating the purging medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cauterization is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Burn the cauterization of how it is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clous" because the head is made in the shape of a nail or has little meat and some gore, and has a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and put on the patient’s shoulder a bandage of pain, and hold your hand and cut off slightly the fever that has come, until the moisture of the spice is dry.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the arteries are not scorched, which is beforehand, and there is abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After placing cotton in the wound area, and putting on a bandage on the patient for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then place wet cotton in butter, and then treat the patient with ointment until he is cured.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cautery called "cultellare", at the tip, and keep the artery covered in this headache which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the head or skull (emigraine in Old French refers to a severe headache)
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you cure an migraine as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and do not take advantage, and see that those who had cautery before told about medicine and iron, did not suffer from it, then it is reasonable to scald the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And so mark on the bone a line with half an inch of length, and put your hand once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and that it does not become just above the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the mandible that mutes when you jaw, and do not let the nerve have sight except for the mute and that spasms do not come to the sick, and be careful of the corruption of the artery when it is cut, or if cutting causes great fear and itself to that who does not know it, and who has not studied and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the work remain in its proper place;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when an artery is struck, and I will show you to them in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that the cautery does not suffocate at the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it in the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said or the chapter of extracting the artery, with the cauterization that has two wounds.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cauterization is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from cold weather
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain comes from cold, and we have used soluble medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pains do not cease, then apply this cautery which is called "poins", because it has this form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After pricking all around the sick ear, or on both sides where the pain holds, and you move a little distance towards the root of the ear then mark it with a pin.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And tie X points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, let it be so that he is sound.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture that must be cured by cauterization is not done except for those that are caused by inflammation, as we have said in the division of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cauterization on appearances that come from drying and phlegm of old men.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this appearance of torture that is caused by inflammation of the head and neck and gargareism, and that one is not worth it, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauters:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one in the root of the ear, and another a little before the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cautery on the part that opens up clean, and they make a cautery directly on the ear above one pore of the forehead and another on the temple as long as an inch.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery there until the moisture of the wound is dried.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is the resemblance of the knife that we have placed in front, but it is a bit more subtle and they should be the larger knives.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment let him be as I have said, until he is clean.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, but if he does not benefit, and the patients do not have fever, then they make four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	On the second joints of the head, and one in the neck, and that which is called "vassels" as we have previously said, and the cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and treat it as we have instructed before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	And to this sickness, it is fitting to give the patient large and flat pills for the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	after taking the head of the patient, and placing the plaster of sainfoin on the occipital region, which is written in treating plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the way of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is so, good is;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if it is not, do III cuts of emollient on the head when you go down to the neck, and give a space between each cut two inches.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and the treatment as for the others, and if you see a jointer (arrow) in the patient's body, then give one cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two cuts on the other two horns, and treat until he is healthy.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and be the cauteries which are called "olive oil" as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is fitting that the head be purified with years and what we have previously stated;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After the examination of the patient, then apply fire cautery to the head and on each corner, and later and thirdly above the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need more, and the body is moist, and the patient suffers greatly, and the disease is severe, then apply four fire cauteries above the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let him wait until the wound is dry, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the treatment until he is cured, and apply the "olivare" which we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of an epilempsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epilempsy doctors should use fire cautery only on those who are flaccid, and it is first necessary to soften the brain by years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, when the patient has great pain and suffers from a harsh remedy.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer, apply gargling and mastication with the brain-stimulating bone marrow often with raw meat;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's head has been cut off and it is placed in a basin, and we do the fire cautery as we have told before, and do the fire cautery on the neck, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is strong and suffers, let him do the fire cautery as I have told to one who has paralysis and softening of flesh, on the spine at the back and neck, and let him do the olive cautery according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, then they must do fire cautery with subtlety according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excessive flow or corrupted moisture and a large fever, then cut off the cauterized parts as we have said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities decline into melancholy and the body of the sick person is moist, then let them drink something because their cerebrum may be purified, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king's head on the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After make a linen band well made, like a circle, if you put it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and bind them so that they do not cross, and keep them well tied from all parts.
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After presenting the bandage, take some melted butter of an old sheep.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and let the heated wood be tempered so that it is not too hot to pour into.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after emptying the circle from within the head, and let it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and make this treatment for the patient each week once with another good governance until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see someone being cauterized while making many pinches all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery is more beneficial to the brain.
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on a moistened cotton cloth in butter and fatty pig's flesh.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eye
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes first through division as I have said, then begin and give the patient a medicinal drink, cleansing the head, and warding off all moisture, and let him sweat or take a bath several times a day.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After he commands him to reapply the bandage, and then make cautery around the head, and make a second cautery on the two temples since there is no aversion in both ears together, or if one has an aversion in one;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	And treat with all the fire cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin, and apply the cautery long according to the size of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And beware of infection, and if you see a lot of blood coming out, if it is stained with poor quality as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incising how to do it carefully.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and there is no case where a cautery or hatereil is applied under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the eyes' shape
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the eyelids are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or on the arteries that appear in front of the chin.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	And we see that this is due to superfluities of cold and moist humors, therefore the fire cautery which I mentioned at the beginning must be done in descending from the eyelids:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	The cautery is applied to the head, and it is cauterized on both the two temples, and on the two bones below.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if it has more sores, then the cautery is made sharp above the eyelid at all small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the flesh by within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	As you take the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit him, then give three bad poisons to the sick man.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After cutting off the head, and doing cauterization on the middle of the olive-shaped cautery;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and do the second cautery on the cautery which is called "clavilis" above the two shoulders, a little below.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and watch that the artery you don't cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by sickness and moisture, then make the cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	This part of the body
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, do the second cautery on the two shoulders as long as the shoulder is.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave my hand except until the third part of the paper is burnt, as I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	one hair that sticks out
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	There is never a case where the hairs of the ointment are converted to pigments, and prick at the ointment, and do a cautery as in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	Instruct the patient to let his hair grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in your own way;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After putting his eyes on a piece of paper like the shape of the fuel of myrrh, and like the beginning of the sign of the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then I put cotton soaked in oil and myrrh from Persile on the wound, then take the cautery of that form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After drawing on the figure a little at a time, and gradually a bit more times, so that the wound is sealed to its place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of health of the work are that you see the paper drawn back, and the hairs raised at the tip of the nail.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and therefore lift your hand, and let it remain for three days, then put cotton soaked in fat until the swelling is gone.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of ointment until he is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if the hairs come back, and the paper is softened then reapply the cautery to the same place, just as you did first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are lost, then cautery until the paper is raised to its natural place, and even, and do not prick at the hair with the nail.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cautery of the medicines burning is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment of the form of the leaf of myrtle;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and live charcoal, one of each.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	And make it fast, if it does not cool, then cover with the form you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and place on paper eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	And if the illness holds only in the oil, then it must be applied with both.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and soak the cotton cloth in oil.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And the patient's joint should be put in its own place and your dough showing on the medicine, press it for a little every time the patient feels numbness of the medicine, as he feels numbness like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, so hold tight to your health.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	When the morsication is not passed, so lift the leg up and reward yourself if you see the paper lifted as it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If it is not so, then put again the medicine on the leg or if the medicine has not worked, until your works are even and your eyes be set straight.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on moist cotton in butter until the wounds are closed, after dressing the leg that is called "dyaflenis" and other things, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to guard your work with great care, so that the wound does not come loose from its place.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes moist after, and the hair pricks in the oil, then resume the medicine on that leg which has been moistened by its own paper, just as you have done before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment until they are healthy.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the poultice of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to these differences your constraints.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and do not be answered the straight path with him who has knowledge of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by fire cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula just as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures are not beneficial, then it is necessary that you make it cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in a clean cloth;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	And bind the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or twitch.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	After putting a damp cloth on the head in olive oil or apple juice.
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After the fire cautery which is thus:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is cut into the cheek so that it resembles the shape of a feather quill, assembled so that the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	so that if you see it, is cut from one cheek to the other, and so it resembles a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but this one is not cut worthily for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the abscess it splits open, and pulling out the pus, and drying;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it opens again, then cut the vein.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After putting on the hot cautery in the shape of a cone, and holding your hand to the cautery at the part of no navel, lest your hands make madness;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And put the cautery in the grease of oil, and it will corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery procedure just before the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this does not work, repeat the cautery once more, and if you still need to do it, then leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After this, put it on moist cotton wool in butter, and apply the cure of the antiseptic ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without being cured, then apply a medicine that is acid and corrosive until the bones are uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and he should follow what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cautery for fistulas that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Treat an abscess and drain the vein;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After, put in the wound a camphor powder of fine quality because this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they put to the amount of a three-year-old child.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and tie your hand firmly, so that the patient's limb does not move at all, unless the blood flows and flows.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is fitting to put some cotton soaked in wine or oil on the wound.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the blood, if it is free from fistula, heals by marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	But if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to administer purgatives to the belly, and bring the fistula back into the body as much as seems proper to him in his own house.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often cavities occur in lips called "poil", and even more often in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cavities of those which we have mentioned in the division, and if the cure does not profit, then apply a small cautery surgical instrument according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	and puts it immediately in those crevices until it comes out from the same place.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after a cure with cerote, so that it may be healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after being softened and putrid and becoming a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	And you cure him just as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Therefore it is necessary that you cut the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the bandage or perforation of the fistula, hold your hand until the iron stays in its place, and pull it out from there;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this again once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in treatments, until he is healthy.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if he is cured thus, that's good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if this is not so, it's necessary to discover the wound and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in his chapter.
dou movement des dens	any movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines and this does not work, then put the head of the patient on a clean surface.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After taking the cautery, which will take shape afterwards in this way, that you put a chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put the cautery hot in that spot, tightly, and keep your hand there so the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After lifting your hand and resume the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After filling the patient's mouth with a salt solution, and then let him lie on his side for an hour and rich fires.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in that manner the teeth that were moving are compressed again, and the gums are restrained, and the moisture is corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When pain of teeth comes from coldness, or there is coldness in the eye, and the medicines have no value, then it is necessary to do cautery according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cauterizing with butter and cauterizing with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterizing with butter if it is done so that you press butter from a vein, and the end in a iron or iron rod;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after pressing cotton and covering it with a cloth over the tip of a tent, and letting the ulcer in butter boil, and applying it to the painful tooth tightly, until it cools;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and so do frequently until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and when you see that there is pus cotton and wool in butter burnt, and apply it to the painful tooth, and put on hot iron so that the fire reaches the top of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	Inassemble the fire cautery so it is made like this that you grasp with one iron chain or twine, and make it thick so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After the fire is applied to the cautery, it will change shape after a while, and then place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do it often, for the pain will be felt on the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	It is fitting that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of applying this cautery, and then takes it out afterwards.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery on your head whatever you want, and according to the power that you have.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	And this is the form of the knife:
des scrophules	dead sores
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrophules (boils) are caused by humidity and cold moisture, and do not respond to digestion by medicine, then use the fire cautery on the hair of which this comes after, and have two openings for the humors to come out from the other side.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and apply the fire cautery on the abscess once or twice, until it comes to a head of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let it be thus for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put a moistened cloth in butter on top of the wound until it is healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a cure, let the limb rest from pains and discomfort until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the ring
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture overpowers the veins of the arm and similarly when it comes from a cold temperament, then it is fitting that the sick person be relieved first with medicinal solutions.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After performing fire cautery at the root of the neck, and being careful not to come too close to the throat, and not burn the wound but only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After performing the second fire cautery at the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and applying the cautery which is called "clavicle" because we have the shape in front.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heal the limb as we have said, until it is healed.
de la toust	of the throat.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and illness of the bone are from moist colds, and the patient has no fever nor sweat, and is the sickness old, then you must II cauters on the knuckle in his joints;

et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and the pins are exactly thirty or more.
