puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper of oil on your left hand if his eyes are to the left, or on your right hand if they are to the right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand if his eyes are to the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if they are to the right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Instruct the patient to put the point of the instrument into the crown by the size of a finger in that bald place on the head where oil is placed near the smaller arm, then pour the instrument called 'almagda' into it wisely, and turn your hand until it pierces into the oil-filled bald place, and feel as almagda comes to the empty thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is fitting that the measure of the instrument almagda be the full width of the space from the prunella leaf to the end of the neck;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the oil crown;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the eye cornea, and then put the instrument next to it where there is water, and press out from one side after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the pain of this affliction has now descended upon him, then let him see the patient in front of him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting for a little while, and if the pain returns, place the force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and does not rise again, gently pull out as much of the pus as possible by turning your hand little by little.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put in water a small amount of the powdered gemstone, and rinse out that oil within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put the oil out by spilling or pouring a clean cloth soaked in olive oil and plenty of lye, and bind with the pure oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	So too, and those of our age, let us put on a common balm with plenty of lye.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the magenta cannot enter into the oil by its hardness, because it has two people who have too hard eyes, so you should take the instrument called "alberit", of which there is this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, and then pour out pus, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and when the work is completed, the doctor attends to it, in case the patient falls asleep on his back in the dark room;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and let him be without any movements, and give him light food, and do not turn his head or arm to the left or right, and tie according to his disposition as if it were three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then let him put it back in the same dark place where he found it, and look at his eyes, and show him some things, and then tie up the wound for seven days.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not for you to do this in the surgeon's office or after the incision now, but rather to alleviate that, because the pain rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if an abscess has come upon the wound, that you put it back into place on the seventh day, and follow the advice of one who knows how to treat abscesses.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is allayed, you put back his eyes and apply some oil to cover his face for one day, and place him in that same dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then he goes to visit her little by little, and she converts herself for her case;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and knows that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And there came one of us who was from the Irrach, who told us that in some distant land someone made a magical piercing to cure the water, but I have never seen it or known about it in our country, nor did I find any mention of it in ancient books.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And this are the appearances of magical forms, because they who do not know them see them.
et soient d’arain proprement:	and seem to be of pure matter:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the heads of the same subtlety, and the backs in threefold angle.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh at the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	No times are born or occur without some joint being dislocated, of which there are many that seem like scorpions at the end.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there is one where it has a scorpion-like joint with red flesh and another with yellowish bone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	Therefore when that one scorpion is soft and not swollen, it is necessary to sit the patient between your hands facing the sun.
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and cover their nostrils, and let the pus run from those scorpions.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then take hold of it with a small spoon so fine that it can be held firmly on one side until you know that the scorpion is completely dried.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	If there is no remaining part that can be covered, if you apply all the subtle treatments lightly, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	But if it does not swell or form an abscess, if you cut as it seems.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if it's malignant abscesses, cut hastily and cauterize as long as the flesh is not stained and are all charred bones, then pour vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the vomit comes and moisture enters just to the face, it is a sign that he is cured.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if moisture does not penetrate as it should, notice that there is bone marrow left in the bones above, because the humors do not come to cut.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	And thus it is convenient to put a small thread of flax in the wound, with needles made of wood, and let no space be left between each one, for it must be at least.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the head of the patient with the thread in his nose for a little while, and treat with an odorant until it comes out through the nostrils.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and often this is done to children at school, and it's a light thing for the one who does it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and examine each in turn by smelling as we are near the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the flesh is not corrupted by it, then pull out the thread, clean the wound, and anoint the thread with Egyptian ointment, and place it back in its original position as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ligaments have completely rotted away whatever is left of the flesh.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	And then apply a poultice of poultice made from onions for some days until it is healed, and if he needs dried remedies, he should use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, because one distills the oils and the medicines or poultices:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be of silver or lead, resembling a lamp with an opening, like a poultice, and the application should be similar:
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if it is a poultice, then make one closed and apply the instruments to purify the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have the maiden hold the head by the hair so it does not touch when one is pouring hot oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh at the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Often there is a disease in the head that is called "telul", and it grows and becomes great boils, until one sees something to behold;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason it is fitting to apply the treatment at first and destroy all the bone, then put on him the cautery or burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays applying the treatment until it becomes large, then take care to prevent its hardness, of red color, poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if one does not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when one cuts it, there comes great mischief to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of a painful touch, not red from blood, and you see what it can be covered, then void the patient and look at the wound with fear, and treat him with dry things and restrain.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When they are struck and pierced
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is known that when a solution of continued continuity comes from one of these old cartilages, it profits little, whether in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	it is therefore necessary to look if this happens to anyone, if you examine whether the wound is fresh with all its blood.
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then add two stitches to the lip, and treat him until he is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are separated on both sides, it is necessary that you burn all the parts of their wound until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a stitch, and tie, and powder above powder of dragon's blood and bruised incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place the powders on a piece of plaster or another kind of plastering material sealing it up, and leave it until it sticks to him, then treat with plasters until he is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The way of suturing if you have to assemble:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we said in the suturing of the belly.
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you before.
des apostemes des levres	of swellings of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Inside the mouth there is an abscess, resembling grains of rice, sometimes small and sometimes large.
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	so therefore you must return the lips and cut each one out, and take it with forceps and pierce into each part.
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then apply the liquid to the wound after the vitreolite incision breaks, until it is stained.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the astringent of asphodel, and cure the wound with drying things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often swelling occurs on the gum after the procedure called "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if it is fitting to hold the swelling with tongs, and cut at its root, and allow the flow or the blood;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the wound the broken vitreolite, or other restraining and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that one returns after the incision, and often happens, when you cut it again, and cauterize.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	If it does not return to its original place after the fire cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	And these are the forms of ulcers for covering.
des sordens	Of sounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Never are assembled at the head of the teeth within the mouth between the gums, rough and painful scales;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	And sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and wormy, until the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth rot.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	If it is fitting to make the patient sit between your hands, and their flesh be in your holy place, and if you remove the teeth or scales appear, as long as nothing remains there;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And do thus for the blackness and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are cleansed;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if one knows that there is at the first reason, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If this does not work, continue to repeat the second day and the second time, until you have gained all back;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and learn that the teeth have need of different forms of instruments to clean, according to what the work shows, because the raspers who have shaved the front teeth have other forms than those who have shaved between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these forms and others are provided for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary to cure the tooth when it is in pain as long as you delay treatment, as much as you can, because this must not be done at all;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is a very high substance, so we have no excuse for the fault.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is forced to have treatment, it is necessary that you be certain about the tooth's quality.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often does the pain trouble the patient, and consider it to be of a saintly nature, and treat the good tooth.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and every remedy will not dispel the pain, as long as the foul discharge is present, because we have already wanted to do those remedies with these physicians;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain of the tooth that is infected, it is advisable to scorch around the entire tooth with a small, strong instrument to prevent the gum from spreading in all parts;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then the tooth will be cut with your two fingers or small tongs at first to clean them well, and then firmly hold the tongs;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	And so let the joints of the patient rest between your own bones, and his body well if it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the right tooth directly into the fracture, and if it does not shoot through, take any of these instruments and pour them inside each part lightly, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the teeth are perceived and broken, it is fitting that you fill them with fabric, in or where they are broken.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you tie tightly with nails, so that it does not break while being tied.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is fitting to apply a great deal of care over the gum for cutting the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take care well that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient by the pain in the root, for greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not do thus as the ignorant masters who by their haste and by their recklessness break the chain, and bring forth nothing but what we have told.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes bring forth nothing but through the stench of this great disease because of the roots that remain, or by breaking the chain, as we have often wished.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the teeth are thrashed, so wash the tooth with wine or apple cider and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if the wound closes with blood coming from it, which often happens, then apply vinegar to cut it.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if this does not work, so cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of ulcers are such that when you first treat the teeth with them, they have long pointed tips and large claws, which do not spread when pulling out the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have large limbs if they do not bend when pulled out, and they should be made of iron well-made, and have teeth to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root stays at the operation site, it is advisable to put some cotton soaked in butter on the wound one day or two, until it becomes moist; and you take hold of the tongs which are called "algefri", because the joint seems like a mouth for care.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they are cut out in this way, as if by a file and it's the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge at all these ties, so it is fitting that you uncover the whole root under which is the tie, and put the instrument which is called "althali", namely plain lance, in order that it is this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And so if it's rough and large if it doesn't break, and if the root jumps at this point, that is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if these do not work, then take aid with all the tools, so that the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument which has two roots, that's the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front on the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, that's the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And if this tool is so strong that it cannot break, and you see that much of the bone remains;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also of other symptoms, which are not described;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters of subtle arts treat themselves with their own instrument, according to what their works and illnesses show, because there are some diseases for which they do not teach any instrument, in case of breaking or other bones, or if it splits, since I told you so, and showed you how to seek symptoms, where is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone, which will not slip, but can hold and remove;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the healing medicine suitable to each one, and if there is rot in the bone, even if it is small, if you have all this instrument;
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not in their natural place and the form is ugly, and even in young girls, it is necessary to know if the teeth are new after the tooth, and are not in their proper position, and you cannot put them there.
adonques lou raie;	so that the edge can be made straight.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is hard with the tooth, take this instrument that has the same shape as the small beak, and is made of good iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file touches and touches in every jaw for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears as if it can be sorted, take a piece of file as is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and is just like the flint with which one makes nails;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in flint, the tooth breaks and breaks with small blows until it doesn't move anymore.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the surface is smooth at the end, and if the teeth are too sharp and it bites the tongue, in order to equalize them so that they don't bite the tongue anymore or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth lock
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the teeth are in the lock, or by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press on that which he bites down with so much pain, and you have treated them with medicine-restraining, and this does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if they are restrained with a thread of gold, because the silver threads rot and decay, but the gold does not move at all;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, in proportion to the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see the teeth, take the thread and double it between two healthy teeth, then tie the knots between the injured teeth, as many as there are, until you reach with precision to the sound tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then resume the covering from just where you started, and strain your hand carefully and gently, until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your limb be tied to the root of the tooth if he cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the flesh of the thread with pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth, and set it so that it does not hit the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then let it set as tight as it can endure, and if he dislodges, or the threads come out, if they are strained with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it remains and serves as such for all its duration, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the address of two healthy teeth, and two missing ones, if you observe:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, so he puts it back in its place, fresh as fresh, just like we said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not let anyone interfere who is not wise and knowledgeable, for at no time was the shape of a tooth made from raw bone, rather he puts it back in its place where the deficiency is, and strains it as we have said, and leaves it there until it heals.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never is a swelling that comes from under the tongue or by nature, as one is born.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a burned wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the wounds are such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and lift their head onto a healthy one, and lift the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	After the cautery, instruct the patient to tie the nerves tightly around the big joint, until the tongue is loosened from its place, and if there are hard swellings or wounds, and it causes sudden pain, then pour oil and strike at the big joint.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the cut is not too deep in the middle part, for the artery which is below.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done that, lift the limb into warm rose water and oil, or cold water, then place the tongue on a linen bandage.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and let the patient with each night lie still in his bed so that he cannot get up.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	and if there is bleeding from the wound, then put on the limb vitriol, which is a burn.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if they do not take their medicine, then the cautery burns gradually, which is good for those who.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then the doctor prescribes another treatment until they are cured.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a black or red color or hardness, so that the patient does not feel it, and do not touch it at all, because it is a chancre;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is leaning towards pus and there is moisture, then take the lump out, and make a cut with a small spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if they do not take their medicine at the right place, then put vinegar drops on it until it is stained, and return to the right place until you treat them thoroughly;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then lift up the limb from the ailment and the disease, and let the healer do other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Evacuation of abscesses from the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	There is no occasion for a throat pouch called "goddath", and properly calling it the two tonsils, and when treating them, as we have said in sectioning, if they are not healed, be cautious:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is hard abscesses of small sense and fusel color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is big, do not touch it with iron, for the same reason as avoiding blood loss.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be left to wither until it dies, and then you will cut it, for if you do not, it will burst on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color and the root is subtle, and you have prepared the instrument to cover, but first examine whether the apertures are closed and smoothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Therefore place the patient in front of the sun, and let his joints be in order, and he opens his mouth, and presses the surgeon's finger between his hands, so that this is the form.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be of silver or subtle gold, as we use cutlery;
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if you pick it on with a needle and the lancet into the almond, and pull out further than you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And take no cloth with you, then cut with the instrument, for this is the form, which seems like force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And all the nails are bent, and one at a time, and they are very good, and made of iron or of bronze;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, cut with shears, so that it is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And it is cut in one way from one side, and another way from the other side.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have cut one of the apothecary's nails, cut the other in the same manner, and after incision, gargle the patient with hot and cold water, and with sweet vinegar, and with dried pomegranate rinds or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the cure must be completed until they are healthy.
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And sometimes new abscesses are born in the throat other than those on the two mandrakes, if they tie them up then just like the two mandrakes tied.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was present in the throat, namely the small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I had tightly closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the canal that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she died if she stayed like that for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high that they had been put in two wounds on either side of the navel.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I then had it removed, and inserted one onion, then put in the fire, and a great portion of bowel;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then fix another part in the other perforated vein, and let the work proceed on the neck, and pressure is applied to the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After injecting one into the abscesses, and cutting a part of it, only a little blood is drawn out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And after thus, the conduct of the throat was cut out in the woman, and now she began to drink cool water and then wine, and did not cease cutting at that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscesses would recur later, and filled up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	So then I placed it and cauterized inside the throat;
ensi demora sens croistre;	The body retains its shape longer;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And separate from these parts, and do not know but that God has made them for me.
de l’uve	Of the ulcer
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When it comes down to the vein, and it is folded back and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if she is too large and rounded, then it is called "vein".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cut just as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit from it, and you see that the pus has been appeased, and it is subtle, then it is fitting to copy it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is rounded together and not long.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	And she is bloody or of a foul color or black, so it is best to remove the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great risk on the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its size and length, to sit the patient in front of the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument with which we made the reminder before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then insert the needle into the vein, and draw it out, and strike at the second and third points that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is best that you do not strike further than the surface that is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you strike too far, it will cause pain to the voice and speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, make use of what we have said about the incising of two almonds, and treat the patient until they are healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of cutting, it is fitting that you use an engine at the cautery of their fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is like water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And thus the patient puts their head on the healthy one, and then presses the tongue against the instrument which we have said about in this cautery, and compresses it with warm vinegar cloth, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using the head of this instrument, because there is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And they put one of their hairs or on the head, and apply the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient is lying on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine within it, without descending to the throat or the spleen;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Instruct the patient to keep their hand in all of the medicine and press upon the eye, the quantity of a quarter of an hour, until you see it congealed and the bites of the medicine are appeased.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see (it congeal), take cotton and spread it upon any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into the cotton canal, until the cotton adheres to the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this frequently, until the cauterization is complete, then leave it to dry, and cast it after 4 days or 5.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have need to reapply the cauterization of the medicine, if it recurs, and after applying the cauterization wipe under the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let them arise from cold water, and let them be cured of gargarems until they are sane.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is more safe than the incision, although it is cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	for when she is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and avrune and similar herbs, and gather them all or any of them in one pot, and add them easily, and boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pots should be well-glued with strong earth, and in each pot there is an instrument of head according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And be it of silver or of tin, and one of the fingers be plunged into the mouth of the patient until the vapour mounts to the eye through the nostril, until the eye is suffocated;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the thing is reattached, it often happens again and again until the wound dries out, and you must be careful not to do this at the beginning of a new abscess, because many things happen there.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do this unless at the decline of an acute abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a needle and insert it into the patient's mouth with an arrow of fire, so that the tongue does not become too inflamed;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the arrow of fire does not give too much grease to the mouth, and this is a good remedy for salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Sometimes it affects the throat as if it were pierced with an arrow or a fish spine, or with nothing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So it is fitting that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun to all the instruments, so that you may see how things move.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what cannot be seen and is returned to the throat, it is fitting that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	In case the thing becomes dry through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cake, or a root of lettuce, or dry bread.
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie the string to the sponge, and then fasten it.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when she comes to the right place, if you see blood, and then pierce her.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come from what we have said, take an instrument of a plug according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And if the curved instruments are in the head so that they can more easily enter into the throat, and hold the head high.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all the blood come out, or push the bone inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and make sure that the patient pushes the instrument in, because he must see if it is moist or if the thing is rough.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if she pushes it out, or tries to push it for the length of the entire instrument, equal in all.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the cauterizing of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	never is medicine given without some medicine, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	When it does not profit at all, then look into the throat of the patient to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound open, then if it has just one small thread or has very fine nails.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	But if that does not work, then take a candle hair, and pour it into the patient's throat, and pour or burn the length of the iron hot, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is poisoned with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take full measure of cold water, and open the mouth, and let the liquid move to the tongue with frequent movements.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if it is quick for the patient who feels the cold, then vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	and if she does not vomit as we have said, then perfume the patient with asafoetida at the instrument I told you about in the fumigation of the nose;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, because she will vomit with tar.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you hold a pot in which there are charcoal sticks, and place it covered with a sieve pierced in the middle, and in that hole, tie the handles of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Instruct the patient to perform his own treatment; and let the head of the cane be placed in his mouth, and close the mouth, so that he does not inhale any smoke, but comes from just outside the nose.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and now the smoke will come out again, and if it does not come out, then repeat the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers from thirst, and eats bitter, salty things, and does not drink any water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and therefore the treatment is that it should be endured for this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the abscess, which is, when it can be seen, similar to curved tongs with pointed fingers that enter the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And take the shape of the beak of the patient, and it has roughness like a knife, so that whatever is taken, it cannot be released;
et vez ci la forme:	and cut in this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The medical practitioner's hand is useless
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many forms of abscesses are found, according to those who have seen them both here and there in this book, and they vary in perforation and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is in two ways, one of which is the same as itself, and due to moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is for when they are inside or in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the abscesses of the head are different from those in the lower body, and the abscesses in the thigh bone are different from those that come into joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if there is no need to pierce an abscess until the bowel is completely dead according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if some of them require piercing while they are believed to be dead, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that occur between joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from the joint, and it is left until it is putrid in that place, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is located near the main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it dies, it will harm the main limb.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	where the ground is weakened so that if you cut into it now it will die.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not fitting to cut an abscess where the ground has already been weakened for digestion, but rather when you are sure that the ground will collapse, because if you cut into it now it will burst open and a fistula will form.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot be cured in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	and it is necessary to know the nature of the perforation of the abscess which dies according to its fulfillment, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the discharge of fever, and the diminishment of pain and redness, and the softening and sharpness of the chief of the abscess, and other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary to situate the puncture or further down from the abscess, and where it opens wounds;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the puncture is long in the body, and if the abscesses are near the hands or feet, or joints, or nerves, or arteries, so that they do not have a vein.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When this part is swollen, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the groin, so that you value (value to leave) the perforation until it is confirmed to be completed digestion accomplished, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce in front of that, the body will swell with the venom from it, and is full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and in case they harden the lips and the innermost part of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is perforated according to the size of the body, according to that which the limbs have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	and it is necessary to tie off small abscesses, small fistulas.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large fistulas, and many fissures according to the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	And if there are such abscesses or it is necessary to cover the wound, and bind.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become so swollen that one cannot wrap it, and is deflated, then it is necessary to do the same way as for the boils.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if some are cut into three parts, and some are cut as the wood of myrtle, just like abscesses from arrows.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if some are treated with a round cut, and other cuts, and similar cutting.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those without a head, like superficial abscesses, it is necessary to let them drain purely.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has collected a great quantity of pus, to let it drain, but not to extract all of it in one hour, but rather take only part of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	And then I have stopped up the abscess just yesterday, and then there was no discharge afterwards.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this gradually step by step, as much as necessary, until the bowel is whole.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Similarly, if the patient has weak virtue, or a woman in childbed, or small children, or elderly men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But the expectation is that it will not occur again at all with the outcome of the bowel, lest by chance the patient dies, and you do not take consolation.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Then avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have pierced the abscess, if it is a wound, and examine whether the wound of the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it's a flat suture, then insert tapes of linen or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it's big abscesses and there is much pus, then it is convenient that you put one tape in each so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have struck a part of the abscess with your finger, and pulled it out, then it is advisable to fill it with old cotton or flannel cloth soaked in moisture, and tie it up just the next day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the bones and the healer of wounds until he is sound.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood comes out of the incision, sew it up with a moistened cloth and linen, and tie on over it repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the veins persist in bleeding, then he must attend to governance and care, and the powders that I have said are in your hands in this book, and if it is winter, and the veins or abscesses are very nervous, then it is advisable to put on tourniquets and moist cloths soaked in wine and hot oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in this state, and the abscess is charred, then it is advisable to put on moist cloths soaked in water and oil, or wine and oil cold, just the next day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then cut the abscess and clean it up and treat it, as needed, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And therefore it is necessary to investigate universally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or, I said that you must look before treating an abscess, and here is the chapter.
des soros	The sorrows
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from on the head, and are of various kinds, like in cloth, just as those from a piece of cloth, or similar to those from a mouse's skin, and there are many such.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are fatty areas and swellings where there is moisture just like in pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And there are swellings that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause harm.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the injuries of the groin are such that if you have found in all the instruments called "entremisoire", of which the shape comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	Because if it contains moisture, they cut through with the long ones.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is empty, if it scorches and there is nothing left to spare the skin that contains the moisture, because it returns when you leave something.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	After plunging cotton into Egyptian ointment if it is present.
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, then in water and in wool, apply the wound, and leave it until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And those who are left after the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the wool, until you know that it will not stay for the night.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with ointment suitable to it, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscesses do not burst out quickly, according to this form for a long time;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	And I pull out your nails, and I scrape off all the skin, and put all your treatment for drawing blood to relieve the chest where it is.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the arteries cause you harm, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus also do with the abscess if it is pained, and as you cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting on the painful abscess and the moisture, if it is lighter, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses or swellings have not been moistened and from those that I copied or swelled the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess in the same way as a stone hard, rough and white, which cannot be broken;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one of them has been burned, it is also as well done a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming or swellings that come on the head of children and the roots of the ears, cut them so thoroughly for as long as possible before they reach a certain point, lest they burst.
et les cure si com il covient.	and let the treatment proceed as it should.
des scrophules	dead sores
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often happen abscesses at the throat, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes appear elsewhere on the body, and are very painful, and join one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And every abscess is located within its own place, just as the wound and the abscess on the head, just as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and there are many similar abscesses.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malignant and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one that you see has good disposition at the shoulder, and is similar to the color of the flesh, silent in all parts and not inflamed at any part or at the artery or vein, nor deeply penetrated.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if it suits to copy it from above, and scrape off each part, and make the two lips pale like veins, if you have need of that, just as we said in incising on the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And then the nail is pulled out little by little, and be sure that you do not touch the nerve or vein, and do not scrape the scab or scratch with needles, lest your hands falter, and see too far ahead, that you may cover more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you touch the vein or artery, and that does not stop, then put vinegar on the wound to break it, or some powder that congeals blood, and bind the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it be so long until the abscess is calmed down and the wound is muffled, and begins to form pus.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Now you wish to know if it will stay there without any small boils or sores, whether it will stop or continue.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if it has a large vein at the root of the boil, so that you will not want to only cut off that boil in its root, but bind with a strong double thread and let it fall down without any trouble;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply a dressing made of wool cloth soaked in Egyptian ointment and then treat the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you strike the scrofula, it is necessary to assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, for there will be no more swelling because of the great size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is necessary that you understand to cut at the root of the thing, and apply force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those boils that have a tendency to burst open, cut into one where it is swollen.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and cut into it as was previously said, depending on the place, and then dress with linen cloth and similar things, so that it does not spread any further decay of what remains.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well cleaned, then the treatment of binding with cloth until it heals.
de squinance	of suspicion
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	They also told and spoke about cutting the throat.
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have strangulated, it is advisable that the cut of the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And do not provide help to those who have cut themselves in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in a state of purging, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to escape the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below three circles or four, one small cut through the middle, between the two circles or according to the size of the cut from the surface, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those who are so sick are very convenient for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the masters are fearful, it is advisable to extend the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then make a cut in the flesh until it comes to the cartilage.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut into the sac, just as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is shown by the section of the throat of the cartilage which comes out through the neck where the law has been broken, and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave a scar over the wound.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour is past because of which we doubt strangulation, assemble both lips of the wounded place with a thread that is whole and soul to the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that make flesh swell until it becomes healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	But do not perform this operation until the throat is entirely stuffed and the patient is judged to be on the verge of death and has begun to fail.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	And thus you must tie the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and so it is kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And because the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the illness has passed, and it passes in three days or four, then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young girl took out a knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the neck hairs.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to cure her, and found her also dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.
