I discovered the wound, and found out that blood had come out of it, and I knew well that she hadn’t cut into a vein or carried it to her neck, but that the veins had burst out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I regretted it, and sewed the wound, and cured her until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the girl that her voice became hoarse, and she returned to her normal state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because of which I thought that there was no fear in the opening of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "gallstones hernia" and it's a large abscess in the color of blackberry, and it's more common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	And occurs in two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	Natural and accidental.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners: for one is similar to swelling and the other similar to an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it is not suitable to apply fire over the fever for one who is small, and he proves and searches at all the interior;
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as similar to swelling, and there is no pain, if you strike it, just like we strike the nail, and take out its entire core, if there is none.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and thoroughly search for all, and let the doctor do it as he knows how, until he is completely well.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of suffering that I will list all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and one must know whether to tell everything, what is the difference between death and discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that discharge is when the fever and boils persist, until the fever has passed and the purulence is complete.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then follows the fever and the cold.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	But with death, there is no cold or fever, nor pain, and it contains its own gallbladder, which is its own sack, and according to the color of the body, and begins like a jelly, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And there are so many appearances, or swellings, or moisture, and much of a color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of one not known, that you examine and inquire first at all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", according as its form comes or to chapter who follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is to take a piece of damp tissue that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers one by one, until you know when the humors have pierced the vein, then only according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the middle part, and be careful that it will not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the abscess bursts in the groin area, cut it according to its color as I said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if there is no moisture after the middle part, see if it is greasy, then cut with a cross, and take out with pincers, and lightly scrape it from each part, and cover the spot where you are treating it so that it heals sound with the wound.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot treat it properly, then cut it by pieces so it does not stay there.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	But if it stays there, it will come back many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	But if it stays for a little while and causes no harm, apply the wound with some corrosive powders, hold it tight, and put on soothing ointments and other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	But if the wound is large, cut off both sides of the wound, and treat the person who has suffered a stroke.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the veins are swollen against this remedy or another, quickly apply the new vitriol splinter, and let it be left for two days or three, until the wound is clean, and allows the blood to settle.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Now the head of the shoulder returns to its place when it has been left for a while without anything.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Now consider the forms of internal swellings, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large and small, and little.
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and in it there are three quarters, which are called "albares", and one that is called "breb", and they are of three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, small, and little, to enclose the sinuses of a fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are just like the nails used to cut splinters, and are made of citron wood, iron, or silver, and they are very useful for those who are yellow, and are more advisable for putting stop to the black pus that fills a fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	And there are three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	big, medium, and small, according to the size of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of ulcers are very similar, just as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	big, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if ulcers have two lobes of the three kinds also.
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if ulcers have three lobes, and are each of the three kinds.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if ulcers have two lobes, one lobe only, and are each of the three kinds.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all these are necessary in their own place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these cuts is made, and it is such that from one side only you cut, so that you burn the nose, because of that one does not pierce the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these intestinal issues are the symptoms returned in handkerchiefs, so that the patient does not experience anything at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they come from three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and you should not cut in only one place, but rather like the joints, such as knees, arms, and breast, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes you make another small instrument, resembling burnt fistulas, according to this shape, because it stains blood;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put him on no occasion by the healthy person who has coped with veins, and arteries, and never again in that great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never are the nipples of any man swollen when they begin to rot, until they look like a woman's.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and keep them swollen and inflamed, and whoever wishes to treat them, if it is believed that the treatment should follow this shape along this line from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrapes the fat, and applies the wound with medicine coated in charcoal, then brings together the two lips of the wound at the seam, and cures until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the nipple turns inward and is swollen as in women, so that it forms two swellings above, then makes two cuts.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is held to the other at its end, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from line b until line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the cautery, instruct the patient to scorch the skin between the two lips, and extract the fat, and apply what we have said about costume and powder, and what is necessary in the treatment, until he is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not healed, or the incision has not been fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the drying of blood, then it is advisable to fill the wound with wet cotton cloth in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let him sit so that the remaining part and the fat are drawn out, then treat him until he is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the joints.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from under the joints are hard swellings or have ribs, and if there is moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those that contain moisture must be closed according to this shape, from the line .b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowel that is in the abscess is empty, apply the wound with old cotton, and let it rest until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment suitable for that until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like swellings of scrofula, do it as we have said in cutting open scrofula wounds, and if the wound has a bowel, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the cauterization of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the veins are cut, and the skin is sewn over it, which often brings forth abscesses, and just as it happens with the vein exposed and an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if it is swollen in the same way as when it is through an artery, because the abscesses are long within;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and if you feel it with your two hands, you will find strangulation;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is due to the vein, it appears as if there are red scars;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is madness to cover up this abscess, and itself when it is under the bones and joints and near the chest, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to abandon the iron treatment, and those with a head injury should also abandon it, and in those who swell from an artery, let them cut through the skin long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then cover the armpit area with linen, and cut off beautifully the artery of the arm, until it is discovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then take off the linen and pierce with a needle at just that spot on the other side, and constrict the artery with a thread twice as thick as two fingers, as I have taught you in the extraction of both arteries found in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then tie the patient who is between the two threads of a ligature so that there is no gap, and remove the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply pressure to stop the bleeding, until the wound stops.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat these wounds so that they heal completely;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it's fitting that you dye your hand with the color of the wound so that you can apply the stain to all the skin, then pour the needle under the part you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and make a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tie the stain, just as I told you, or tying of one part of two threads of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the threads won't set in, then pour another needle over all the thread under the entire stain at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until it stops bleeding, then cut off the excess skin and leave what's tied.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put it on my drapery moistened with wine and oil, then apply treatments of poultices and bandages until he is cured.
des apostemes des ners	From the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	When an abscess comes from the artery and vein, it comes to the nerves when they are dried up, or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the joints and in the bones where there are wounds, and it's like an abscess, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and there is more disposition to die from pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one is stretched to the point of pain, the patient feels pain, and it's not just in the wound, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and he is mute from all parts, and cannot go forward or backward, neither above nor below, and one who has dislocations should not cover them with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	perhaps he will experience contractions;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and they who are on the head or on the forehead, do the skin at the spatulate.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If there is an abscess that is small, if you have nail clippers, and cut at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if the surgeon takes out the tumor and scrapes it, then he fixes the wound to the ribcage, and continues the treatment until the patient is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Never does it happen in the belly and not in any other place, for it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to fungus, with subtle roots, and large thorns;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and in it are both small and large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	In the house where there was one woman who had two swellings in her belly which were more like fungus than any other thing, and she didn't have a difference between them, they were white, and had small roots, and had split open, and decayed with moist air.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I copied them and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other 6 ounces, and the work in the incision is such that you look to see if the patient has moist wounds, and the color of the armpit is white and moist, with a fine root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If you cut it with a large spoon or spatula, and it is in your sight, the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For when cutting comes the many great hemorrhages of blood, and if you do not watch yourself, then hasten therefore to the cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient with fear and anxiety at the incision of iron, if you take a long and well-made thread, and bind the arm so as we have said, and let him rest for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it tightly, and do not cease to tighten the long thread until the arm stops hurting and feels better by touch;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, and there's fear of cutting into the same place on the abdomen, but you must cut half of it, then cauterize so it does not return;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and keep in mind that you should not cut into the red tissue which is of fresh color and has poor sensation and runs with milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an enchantment of an abscess, and I have come to this cure for the chancre after.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil exists.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a wound comes from cautery of a cut or incision on the scalp, and is in the abdomen with some swellings as in other cases, or from blood that cuts through veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by scalp incision and from the intestine's issue, since the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing with pain, and opens to various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the outcome of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press on both sides so that it returns, and then comes back, and by chance it gets scarred, and becomes much larger at the entrance to the bath and for great work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it's because of moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it's because of blood, it opens by these signs the big and hard abscesses, and are stuck in a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it's due to weakness, then it's soft at the elbow, and if the wound is examined to see if its appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or the vein, or weakness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it suits you to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the gallbladder, it is advisable that you instruct the patient to tie his groin and be stretched out straight, then stitch everything around the wound.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then instruct to sit sovereignly between your hands, then go around the patient that you have stitched all over the stomach area, and then stitch half of the abscess on top with great care.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie around with a strong thread or a cord of very strong silk tightly, and make sure it is fastened well on both ends.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then open up half of the abscess and extend it on the ligature, and pour into your wound the intestines;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught on the ligature, pull it loose, and pour the intestines into the outside of the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, pull it out on the onechene and cut off its surplus.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the arteries cause counteraction, or the vein, then go smoothly into them, and return to your work and take two needles, and pour two thick threads, and pour the two needles back in the place where you made the puncture.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in four fingers above the needles, and if you see it, pull out the needles, and leave it to him as long as he suffers, and cut the dead flesh by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	When you strike at it when it is subtle and bloody, then the surgeon does what is required, and he cuts open the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And extract the blood or moisture you find, then treat the patient with what is needed, and bind the limb.
dou chancre	dough chancere
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division regarding the symptoms of a chancre, and how to treat it with medicine, and how to avoid using iron treatment;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	And the chancre spreads to the groin, and great care must be taken in its treatment, and the ancients said that when a chancre appears on the person or can be removed like one in the testicles, or in the groin, or in similar places, and it should be completely removed as soon as it appears at the beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	And when it is great and old, so do not approach it, for I have never seen any of the sick.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	I have never seen anyone cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the abscesses, when it is in its place or can be removed, as we have said, are that you never purify the sick person of black bile.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him healthy if he has shown signs of excess, then cut the abscess.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then throw away your ulcers or cankers, and cut off the head from all parts, and remove the bone from all parts with nothing left.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow out completely, and hope well with your hand or with something, but if they begin to bleed again from the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize so that the skin is not washed.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the patient of another treatment until he becomes sound.
de ydropisie	From dropsy, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	As we have said in the division, the signs of dropsy and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each one, and the cure that is done with medicine, and also that which is cured by iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if only it is blistered;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and iron should not be touched in these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and yperochia, because it is a mortal thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore when you give medicine for this similarity of dropsy called "blistering" and the cure does not work, then look at if the patient is weak or if he has another disease than dropsy, such as stomach troubles and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If it has not been touched with iron, because there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see a patient of great virtue, and he has only dropsy, but is not too thin or too tall, then so treat him:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lift the patient upright over your hands, and have the attendants press his belly down to the lowest part of his stomach, then take the thorny spatula in that form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so are the rules of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	with a point, and make sure it's not too deeply inserted so that it can come out at the intestine when you throw it in, and do not squeeze.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look to see if the dropsy is tied down towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If you must break open (open) in such a place, since it is a third tooth, you must cut downwards from under the jaw.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropiness is due to liver disease, then if you cut to the left of the third tooth;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to mucous, then if you cut to the right, and do not allow the patient's blood to flow onto the wound that superfluous humors run towards the weak part of him;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and the point, and lift your hand to all the spatumile between the skin and the sac as if you were scraping it out with the quantity of an fingernail or two.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the sac until the spatumile comes to its natural place, and that is the liver, then take out the point, and use this instrument which has this form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is like a silver chain, so fine and subtle, and made of iron or anvil light, and in the lower part there are small holes.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on the other side, three holes.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	And two on one side, and one on the other.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And the knives are cut like a pen, and it is the shape of the incision that scribes write on the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the top of which is the hinge, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it now turns upwards on the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	then it is cleared half or two-thirds, for if you clear more than it is fitting in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the solution of his spirit with the arm, or he will let out hands, or he draws near to death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but when it is clear according to the amount of his virtue, and according to what the disposition of the virtue tells us about the patient's feet;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then take the instrument and hold the water, and now it is held in place by the dressing which stops up the puncture that is on the sac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then take up the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and take a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this on another day, and be careful not to fool around until it doesn't last but a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	and if you doubt the patient, and take a lot of water, if the treatment is to the dust or cold stone, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and they drink a lot.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and instruct the healer to dry out the patient with medicinal desiccatives until they are healthy, and cautery on the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	There is never an infant born without any swelling in the penis, or if there is swelling, it is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it seems that soon they will pierce at all the sensitive places, very subtle and according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or pierce with a subtil (small) bone of a plonc ( probably a type of fish), and tie it up thus for three days or four, when he wants to make urine, if the stitches are made loose, then make urine again, and then put them back.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and in case it does not come out at all, because the urine that comes is not the one he left closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is in his foot, then put on a tunic made of thin cloth, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the piercing in their own place are sick, because no one is born with a piercing at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate before they lift their penis up.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot move for this reason because the material cannot come to that place, and it is a bad sickness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies on his back, put there is a point from the head of the rod and it strikes just as long as the space of a grain of millet, so that the puncture occurs in the middle, as it should.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and keep away from the consequence of blood that comes often, and if it has happened, so that the stain that causes the bleeding stops, and treat the wound until it is clean.
des pustules de la verge	from pimple of the prick
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Often come cysts on the rod, and it is a bad appearance.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malignant and non-malignant ones.
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	If it is necessary that you grasp them at the base one by one, and strike and crush all, then put on cotton moistened in Egyptian balm.
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the ointment again and again until it is made pure.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the bath is malignant, of a foul odor and stench, it is fitting that you should apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you strike them and the fat is in the wound, if it has both inside the skin and outside, if necessary, you should remove the fat that is within first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when it is soldered, remove it.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	Because when you treat the whole area together, if you don't take care to secure the joint of the vein so it is not perceived, and pus and corruption come into the vein and on the spot.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	if it is necessary to shave all that which is black and rotten, then tie up the emplaster of honey and flour which shall be made from the rind of greengage plums and walnuts, then cure other cures until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if they bleed from the wound comes, so apply lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The fire cautery is beneficial in both the assembly of limbs.
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	this means, at the decomposition and corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the joints of the finger are corrupted and contracted, if it is necessary to put or apply a bandage around the finger made from wood, and let the patient urinate among them;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hair grows again to the head of the finger where it has become infected or for an abscess, if it is necessary then that you burn it with a scalp instrument until the ties are loosened, and deliver the joints of the finger from all parts;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	And if this is a grievous thing to consider, then it is proper that you burn at the spot on the head of the spine with a thorny staff and some poultice.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then serve it well between the second and first joint, with some linen thread moistened with cold water, so that it adheres to the bone.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is no less of a concern for continued bleeding as other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	It is good to take care when we perform this work of our own will, and especially in children, for it is proper that the one who makes them should do the best and most gentle work for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say that circumcision was done for their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	Because I have sought the greatest part of the masters and physicians who performed circumcisions around the umbilicus, and with force, and for all those who are weak.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If it is swollen because of the knife because he has two boils, and by chance if one pricks those above and doesn't move until they grow.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Or the wound covers again, and there is double pain, and with the rubbing that does not remove the doubt about the sharpness of the point of the member;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and with the rubbing of the ulcer by chance the iron escapes, and it runs over, and many times this happens as if they need further rubbing and I have tried it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is made with force, all along the whole tendon of thread I have found the good fortune of the experiment, because the forces cut exactly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, the fingers become equal in length in all things;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the hair is well straightened inside the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and if the manner of the first operation is that you make think the child, if it understands, to do only tie the thread around the stick so only, and then make joy in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then make it straight with your hands, and set back the strength between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the limbs.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then dip your hand in the horn and breathe upon it, and hold it up so that the joints of the horn are uncovered;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled upon it, then tie it with a new linen strip doubled twice, and tie it under one thread to another thread;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	And tie it tightly with two threads on the second hand to the bag and the tube, then sew between the two threads, and lift the wound hastily and take off the head of the horn;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	Then let the blood flow slowly, for it is the mother.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on it and above the powder I made glue from a half-moon of fat cooked until it is still warm with rose water, congealed with good olive oil and fresh, and let him lie on it for another day, and the doctor will treat him again till he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of forces at mortification if it is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The two shoulders shall be joined together and tied up tight; and the shoulders should be as large as the right arm.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the fault in the cleansing of the wound occurs when the knees within are pierced by the incision.
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then you should extend it to your angle, so that the wound is opened.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold to your angle, take the nail and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	and if they stay for three days and that which is under the girdle is swollen, let it be left until the wound is cauterized lightly.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you cut as you move, and keep away from the girdle part, it will do no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Cure then the joints of those who have sudden pains from powder, as we have said when treating powders, and if they strike too much beyond measure, and it goes up, so it does not harm anything.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure him, as we have said, until he is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	When retention of urine occurs
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to the stone, or blood clotting, or phlegm, or gall, or similar things that we have discussed in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not flowing, and you see that there is retention due to a stone that is lodged near the neck of the bladder, then it is convenient for the patient to sit on his heels;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and place the stone on his back, and extend his belly from above his back, and restrain the patient as much as he can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And therefore it is constrained to pull the joints of the bladder towards the expression of the stone above, because the urine is loosened.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if she does not come as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, so it is necessary to administer an extraction for all the instrument called 'siringue', because of which there is a swelling:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it should be made of fine and light silver wire, like a bird's feather;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and the size of half a palm and half an inch, and be fine at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the way to extract urine if you take a single thread, and tie a small piece of wool or cotton at the head, and pour the head into the siringue;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	Let the excess moisture of the linen be coped and the balm applied to the head of the siringue, then oint the siringue with oil or butter and with mallow and wine, and sit the patient on the chair, and make him lie down the belly and the verge of oil moist and oil of olive and water tede;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then lay the siringue slightly in the verge, until it comes to the root of the verge, then double the verge upward over the wound;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then pour a balm on the siringue before it reaches the belly, and the patient feels it coming up to the empty place, for that is not done according to this order because of the direction in which it is going is twisted;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then let it stand for a little while, and the thread will come out to every strand of hair, and the urine will follow the urine, then pull it forth, and make the urine run.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and begin again with the syringe as long as the bladder is empty, and set right the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Of urinary afflictions
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or pus is in the bladder, or when putridness is assembled there, and you see blood and medicines distilling out, do this to all the equipment called "clepsedre", and it's the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	This one is closed, and if it's three perforations,
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see.
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the leaden pins because the medication is cold, so that it may warm up well in the penis, if we can put an application on the moisture, and push when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see that your medicine is in the bladder, put on the head of caustic in the moisture, and pull out as far as it will go.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you touch the moisture to the healer, and then tightly close the wound;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	If the moisture enters in, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of a subtle cyst, which is what we call a bladder stone:
si est ci:	if it is there:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And if it is made of silver or lead, and the joints are higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below at the spot where the ligaments burst;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	Then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you see used to treat the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a good double thread, and heat the bladder with this warm moisture on the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Now the head of the shoulder into the fistula, then strain your hand on the bladder until all moisture has arrived at the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle around it and pierce it all around.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then tie the thread tightly through these perforations, then assemble the circle as you would the nail and put within it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and attach to the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do it in the same way as you did with the bladder of your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already discussed in the division the methods of stones and the extraction of assemblies of medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And I said the difference between a stone in its socket with water, and all signs, is that one which should be cut.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the phallus;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	And I will tell you about it explicitly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone stuck in the bladder often occurs in children, and it is a sign that the water has escaped from the bladder like water escaping into its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and I have shown them, and the ailing ones complain about their phallus, and they often pierce it many times, and then inflame.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and because of these frequent attacks the foundations are worn out;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is light in children until they are four years old, and is very much grieved in the elderly, and is at a middle stage between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and it is the easier cure for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with catheter, in order to clean all the filth which is inside the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	But there is no use when it comes to cutting the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the hands and stretch and move down below, so that the stone descends into the bladder to the bottom, and does not fall back up into him.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his knees, so that the bladder is entirely sloping downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	and then touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel a stone in space, then get up now to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it doesn't come out at the toucher (the spot where you cut), so that all is moist with the oil of your left hand, then let the patient be ill, or to his right side, if he is an old man.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	And set the bow in its foundation, and choose the stone, and when you feel it on your left side, if it is thin at the base of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on to your left side, and set the bow at the door where you will be cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and he orders him to stretch out his right hand to the top of the fingers, and his left hand to remove the leather below the fingers in the place where one makes the cut;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then I pour the salt mixture onto him, because this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And they put it between the joints and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left knee;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and it should be straight above the stone, and its two ends at the foundation, and if the passage is too wide due to its size, and inside it is narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	in case the pressure from the two ends that are at the foundation causes it to break or shatter.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and search where there is part of the stone with angles and margins;
si est griés a issir;	if it is stuck to come out.
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And if there is an ulcer at its root, appearing like a splinter, and resonating, from which comes light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Therefore if it has angles and borders, make the incision larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	And if it does not heal, if it is fitting that you strain the nails which are like a file on the head, to press and squeeze the stone so it will not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you pour in a small instrument curved at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot put it in that way, expand the puncture so that the pus comes out, and if the nerves are not cut open, squeeze it with vinegar.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more stones, pour in the largest one into the neck of the bladder first, then cut it up, and the small ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or his urine comes back through because of that which his bowels cannot hold.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but one should exert oneself to treat, or to debilitate with nails, until you treat it by pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood and strain it, and bind with wet cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and red rose water and cold water to cool down the swelling.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then revive the patient on his neck, and do not unbind the bandage until at least three days have passed.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, so that the joints are freed from their pain and evil, apply a great amount of oil and water to the healing place, then apply the ointment of infallible and the ointment of basilicon until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And when an abscessed foot comes to the wound and corrosion, and freezing of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this, the urine, which is known in a certain manner without falling with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	But therefore cut the vein in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains, the bladder will corrupt, and it will rot.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound with water and bandages and cloth, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	It is convenient that all the remedies you cure him with, you tie the two knees and assemble the medicines on his body.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small and it is embedded in the bone, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the cure of what I say is so that you cut your tail, then you are excused from cutting for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron according to this shape and fix three nails into the one bone.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie around the vein next to the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then pour in the forest (blood) gently into the vein, until it comes to the stone.
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	And turn the forest (blood) in your hand towards the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If blood comes forth soon, then press your hand upon the thing that is left behind of the stone which is inside the vein.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it breaks forth soon and comes out with the urine, and is healed, then the patient will be cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do that for any reason which prevents it, then tie the foot below the knee and the other above, then make the stick straight between the two joints, then pull forward, and release the joint, and clean the wound with ice that is in the injury;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let him remain as long as he is cured.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone in women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	There is little chance that a stone will be embedded in a woman, and if it has happened once, the treatment is painful and is forbidden for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman knowledgeable about how to remove stones, especially when she is cast away.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art with her hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth manner is that the femur of a woman is deeper than that of a man, because it can be made to have a deeper shape, and great fear there is. And if necessary, you should seek out a midwife well-versed in this art; at any cost, find one true, and if you do not find her, then use some subtle trick.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and presents a well-known woman skilled in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of this art, and commands that she do what you command regarding the cutting of the femur.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and examine her very well to see if she is a virgin;
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	And then he must put his hand on something firm, and look for the stone.
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And if it is true, then he must press the arm with his left hand against the belly wall.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	And if it is true, then he should move it from hard to hard, starting at the entrance of the bladder until it reaches the root of the thigh.
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	Then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh, against the midpoint of the bone, where it has been moved and feels the stone in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	And do not move his hand above or below the stone, and let it be fixed at the first small mark.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	Now put the bone in its place in the belly, if you feel a stone very close to the wound so that the stone can come out fully, and find out what many kinds of stones are:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	This is to know that there are small and great stones, sharp and blunt, long and round, and those with holes.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the similarities to determine the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if they do not contain poison, then apply vinegar to the wound and hold it for an hour until it is stained.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	Then return to your work until the stone comes out, and have the purulent substances which I told you in the extraction of stones to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	And if they do not contain poison, and it is the artery that has been cut, apply powder on the wound and put the purulent substance of lentils and bendels, and do not start again with this, and leave the stone alone, lest the patient die by chance.
puis cure la plaie.	Then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is calmed and the pain is overcome, so that you return to your work, until the joint is restored.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia in the groin.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	The rince water is nothing other than the assembly of moisture or white phlegm, which is below the level of the joints, that contains the blood.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and is called "phlegm", and it is never properly in the blood itself, if one thinks that this is another blood.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it's the skin of the joint between the white phlegm that we have said.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	This does not happen.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this mucus is weak that it comes to the joints, and spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And at times if comes by percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it's yellowish decline, or without red, or black, or white waters, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	For it is the sign of knowing this assembly, for when it is white and swollen as we have said, if there are abscesses that form, it looks like an egg, and does not open because of moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in its own skin, there are abscesses that form with a part of the egg, and because of this one thinks it's another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the joint and the swollen part, it feels warm.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you see the color of the moisture, it confirms that the swelling is at the inner quarter circle, and so the form is as expected.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Then according to what comes after the surrounding area, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cut with iron, it is fitting that the patient be made healthy according to our skill and the fullness of their body.
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	Then let the swine lie on his back, on a thing one foot high, and put many folds of cloth on him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	Then have him lie on his left side, and instruct the minister to have him lie on his right, and stretch the stick towards one of the two ribs near the breast;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula and cut the skin of the breast from his long line to the joint, and make a straight cut through, dividing the skin just so it is white as snow, and scrape off thinly according to one's power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the white spot flat with water from the great puncture, and extract all the water, and then put on your bandages, and stretch the white spot upwards;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	And do not touch the heart of the joints, but only the surface alone.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cut or cut him entirely as well as you can himself, for if you do not cut it correctly, he will return to the illness.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	And if the ulcer bursts forth at your work, then remove it to its place when you have completed the operation on the surface.
