puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then join the two joints at the heart of the joints with a bandage, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the ulcer corrupted by another disease, it is wise to tie up those suspensory bands, doubting the progression of the bleeding.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cut the crown at all the surrounding skin, and extract the blood, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if an abscess is assembled in two parts together, saying that these are two foci;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if cut the other part just like you did on the first one equally, then clean the blood and put linen moistened in rose oil on the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another linen moistened in wine and oil over it, and on top of the two wounds, and cover them with double clothed dresses, and tie it up above all according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take the two cloths and fill them with wool fluff according to this resemblance and assemble them by sewing in the neckline of the braies, and one of the shoulders takes hold on the foundation just as high as the back, and the other at the part of the nail;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	And the other two joints on either side of the heart, are all tightened together in a knot of the arm.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And at no time is medicine applied with the cautery of fire in place of iron, and then you must grasp a subtle cauterizing instrument, and strike the skin of the joints, and it should be heated as we have said, so that the white sac which contains the liquid is exposed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery in this form, and pierce that sac at the joints, and scorch it with this subtle cauterizing heat:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And strike him in all the ways you can, until you have scorched him thoroughly;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and keep so that the fire does not touch the eye;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	And therefore knows that this work is more safe;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and must keep watch against the occurrence of bleeding, and women must be careful with the work of amputation;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if no other thing contradicts you, or an abscess occurs, or bleeding or any other thing, then cure what is contrary according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and will not endure this work because of its horror, then perforate him as I have said, and when you are certain by the meanings we have explained that water is laid into a wound, then place the patient on the raised seat.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess at the lower part and as far in as the entire surface of the limb is wide, and make the perforation all along the long length of the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	And if they are large wounds, so that all of the fluid flows out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton over the wound, tie it tight, and let the remaining fluid drain off, then cure until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white linen cloth does not allow the fluid to escape from the wound in the mouth of the wound, then it is wise to insert a quill or the instrument used to treat the swelling, for this form should be as before;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound, and see that the fluid returns, and is assembled again after six months or more, in which time it will be as before, and so the patient's days will pass;
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses on the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	see that in the cutting of this branch there is great fear of more deaths, because it seems to me that one should not cut;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you about the wound and its symptoms.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	Therefore, most wounds come from the body, and similarly have veins.
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it's because of a lot of cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	which is known to be through excessive acidity and sharpness, which spreads in the veins, or by percussion.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and is the color of the wound according to the color of the body.
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	does not bring pain, and is a painful wound.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and sometimes is a painful wound with purulent and bloody color, and at no time comes from another artery, or swelling of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is through no artery, so is seen by the shape of the abscess, when you press on your two fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and do not touch anything else.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is swollen with blood is known by its shape at the expression of gentle pressure on the two fingers, and it can be easily felt above this appearance, and above other swellings;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And so you hit the thinnest part of the vein, then pierce the top, and pull forward the flesh, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the vein is already swollen with these swellings, then it is necessary that you treat the vein and hit it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is in the sac or inside the vessels, so that you can deliver all that place and return smoothly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the hair of the arm is at their backside, it is fitting that you copy it all and extract the pus, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your operations are completed, apply the wound of woolen cloth in oil rose and wine, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses on the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess that has been enveloped and wrapped around like a calf's udder, with the softening of the tissues, and the patient suffers greatly when it ruptures.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment for this disease is just as painful as that which was before, and we will tell you about it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	You must place the patient on the raised table, then pour the liquid of the vessels down to your knees, and all the surrounding flesh you will stretch out, and spread it apart.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut with the scalpel deeply through both sides of the wound, until they are exposed, and then clean each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then prick an arrow or place a double thread at the place where the vein has come out, and tie it to the first limb above, and tie it closely under the other limb;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut in the middle straight on, according to the length of the body, and pull out the corrupted moistures;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound just as with others, or burn with arrows, so that no vein comes to flow;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because through this no harm comes, and the veins come to all of them, so it is fitting to treat the vessels for all of them;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	If the blood does not stop flowing because of the incision on the vessels, and dries up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	From the operation of the scalp
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The venous distention of this type occurs by the cutting that comes out through the suture, or the extension on the abdomen in the region of the kidneys, because the intestines descend from that incision to one of the veins.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this incision is either on the suture, or from the extension of it, and these two manners come about from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or from percussion, or a fall, or a burn, or the lifting of pain, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is an extension of the suture, are that there are little by little, in long time, and do not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and it is the abscesses equal to its place up to the point where the syphilitic advances the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it's from the scalp section, that it brings sudden pain at its beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, under the skin close to the bone, and this is because of the intestine's movement and the body's avoidance of the scalp incision.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes he ties the intestines around it, and is retained in that place, causing great suffering to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And for iron cautery, because of fear, he would rather shun it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the way of opening the abscess is that you instruct the patient to insert his hand into the intestine at the wound, if it can be returned.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then sit upon your navel between my hands and lift up the testicles;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then press the heart upward, and cut through all the skin of the joints until long.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then pour into the belly of the navel a string according to what you have need for to open the wound, and so that they can be pulled out;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scorch the syphilis that is under the skin of the joints until the white syphilis becomes visible from all parts;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	Then pour your thumb index into that place which indicates the joint, in that place which is between the white shoulder blade and under the skin of the elbow, and between the second shoulder blade, and from that which is behind the elbow, and between the second shoulder blade;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And then move your right hand inside the joint, and let the white shoulder blade be above your left hand, lift the elbow to all the shoulder blades towards the chest;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And instruct the minister to extend the elbow upwards, and release that which is above behind the knot;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And ask your two to see if there is any intestine protruding or white shoulder blade inside, and if you find nothing, then blow into the belly under;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	Then take a needle or one with a big thread made of X threads, and the bottle in the back part near the flesh.
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	After the incision, then cut the hairs that appear with threads, until there are IV threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	Then gather them together in a cross shape, and bind the flesh where we have said is underneath the skin of the joints with a strong cord of two parts.

et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put the tying in that place according to the first tie long two parts of that one, and then after these two ties leave some flesh underneath the skin of the joints large as two fingers.

Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes cauterize the white flesh sac that we have said to be done after incising, by doubt of the slowing down of blood.

puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another remedy until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia in the groin.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this chapter I have never seen anyone who dared to do the cure with iron.

Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilitic is constrained, and has no appearance in the routine, and the cautery is more moist in this location, and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin on the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Sometimes the hair of the groin in some men is made soft because those hairs are softened, and it can be seen.

puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	When the cuts between the ribs are opened, and the treatment is done as with other wounds, until he is cured, and the wound is closed with thread.
dou chastrement	doubtful pain
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Since certain armor is prohibited by law, and that is why I do not wish to discuss it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and are necessary for only two purposes:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one is that the mirror will be able to tell us how to answer when one is asked, and in order to know the cure;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other is because we have often had to do armoring of certain beasts in order to help ourselves, as with oxen and sheep and cattle and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that armor is done according to two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	Out of attraction, or out of cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one we make by attraction, we sit them in hot water best, until the joints are softened and for as long as.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	Then press them with your hand, until they are set and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	On the operation of amputation:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is fitting that you tie the best bandage, and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then secure the suspension, and cut off each one as you have well washed.
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave no small space on the surface that is under the vessels;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of cauterization is more painful than that which is done by attraction, because at the attraction sometimes something from the wounds remains, because of which the beast desires luxury;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	regarding those with both sexes
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	there are two kinds of hermaphroditism, according to two types of bodies:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is that between the two sexes are open like the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes its urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is in women, and it has on the nail as if a finger, and two wounds.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of the male and female conditions is that you copy the joined limbs in all, and the treatment as if it were other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second manner, of men whose urine leaps out from the skin, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tooth.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	The part of the tenticle is stuck to the natural place, so long as it is too ugly to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it too much with one hand, and that's the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary to dye the surplus of the tenticle with your hand or on one side, and cut lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not go too far in the wound, lest blood comes and stains it, then the cure will need another cure until they are sane.
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and to another charm that is born at the mouth of the mare's womb, and the navel, and by chance it will come forth, and they call it according to its resemblance like a cow, and for this they called it "the cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it must be copied, as we have said about the testicle, and the treatment until it is healthy.
de erratique	of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Misjudgment occurs when the nature of a woman is not recognized, or the loss is sought.
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	And it comes from her natural birth or accident by illness that has happened to her.
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	Or it comes from a collision of bone, or by subtle or deep dislocation, and is made inside the marrow, on the ribs, on the side, or in any other place;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and prevents conception and childbirth, and by chance may also prevent flowers from growing.
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	And knowledge of this is acquired through the reflection of a fall.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If there are recent symptoms that appear, then either in your right side or left side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is a subtle dislocation and the joint is near the two fingers, make haste to treat it accordingly.
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Put your two hands together, and let the woman lie on her back, with her legs spread out.
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	Then let the two fingers form a circle, until the subtleties are rinsed and the sponges are saturated.
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take wool and the mucus in oil, and put it on the wound, and have the woman rest at home every day, so that it will not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syfach is hard and dense, it is fitting that you cut with the spatula like a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the sponges are made of charcoal, then remove them after an hour and again after a day.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	And apply the medicinal salves, if you like, such as saffron blood, dragon's blood, incense, and many other unguents.
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	After a cauldron of fire is brought to a boil, so that the wound cannot be closed;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and then they let it dry for a long time, and they place a linen tent on it.
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat other remedies until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes a hare, then they should cover it according to this manner, if it is not an enchanted spell.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the apostles that are in the marsh are not to be touched with fire.
des emorroides	wounds from hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Emorrhoids are openings of veins that occur without any condition, and when old hemorrhoids form, they become tumors.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	And as we have previously discussed in the division the symptoms of oars and signs, I will tell here those that receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and ulcers when they are completely filled in the marsh and do not appear to the touch, unless it is with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the mare can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is therefore necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then wait for the ulcer to appear again, and cut it out with tweezers, and dig at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, as does ace and saffron and incense, and similar things.
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	Then put his feet in cold water for an hour, then put him in cold water.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	And if bleeding occurs again, so that he falls, then make him sit in a decoction of sumac and apple peels and gall, and then give him flour of rye, mix it with honey and easily, and then apply it to his back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she stops bleeding, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If this does not work, if you make him hang (or breathe hot air) on the back and to the nipples so they will hurt.
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take linen, and apply the poultice in juice of plantain or aglet (or elder) with wine vinegar, and make him breathe on it.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess rests, then treat the wound of ointment until he is healed.
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	And she who is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a harsh head, so they cover it like I have said.
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the cure until he is sound.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the marrow, such as chancre and abscess of the bone, herpes, eczema, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and other diseases that I have mentioned in this division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary that I write in this treatment the abscesses which come on the marrow, which are not like other abscesses that are made by a bow.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you see the work of iron, look to see whether the abscesses are thick in its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you will know.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore do not hasten to pierce it, but let it be treated until the pain is eased;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	And then sit the patient on the bed, and have two stools or chairs where he leans, and support his back and assemble his feet so that they are away from the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and spread his thighs apart, and put his arms below his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then draw the bowstring over his right side, and insert the instrument used to cut open the mouth of a mare, because that's what will come next.
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you insert this instrument, you fasten the string first to know the depth of the mare's mouth, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the swelling is greater, so it is advisable to cover with a deep layer of drapery, so that the swelling does not trouble.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is advisable to put the horn of the instrument on top, and to sharpen the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess is opened and one strokes it with the thumb of the hand, they consider covering the forehead, and the spatumile (a type of spoon or ladle) with water.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the arrow is empty, it is advisable to put moist swabs in the wound in olive rosed oil or dry olive oil.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the moist cloth of the wound on top of the deep layer of drapery, and cover it with the surface without drapery, and over that, place a linen band clean and moistened in water or honey (soaked).
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	After two days of applying treatment, it happens to him.
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and no time is lost to apply poultices and wounds by a compress of water and honey, and then boiled herbs like myrrh are long cooked.
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	and then reapply the treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is covered with linen, so it is fitting that you should be careful not to apply hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	The first thing is to look at the belly that she knows the shape of the child, and the signs if you see the woman press her nails, and desires to sniff the air:
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	so then one hastens for the infant to be born.
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	so then you know that this child is according to the natural shape, and is born from his head, and the second comes with him.
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	And when you see these signs, it is advisable to press lightly on his belly, so that the fever passes quickly.
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	because when he descends to his head, he brings with him the second joint, and the sinews of his superfluities are cleansed by good cleansing.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this which comes in another way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	Because it comes sometimes to his feet, and comes forth from the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes to his belly, or else, and is changed by chance upon his neck, and by other evil figures.
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	so it is necessary to the physician that they be wise and subtle in these things, and avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures by which one must assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the patient comes down with a fever due to natural cause, and the woman in labor groans, and the virtues of her are weak, then she should be placed on a horseback, or the women hold her;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and let her oil or fenugreek be cooked until it is done, and then pour the bile between her two nostrils with the small spatula which is this shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and cut the tendon, and strike at her joint until the moistures that are within it dry up;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press the belly of the woman until the fever subsides, and if it does not subside, then it is fitting to bind the woman with muskillaige (or fenugreek) salve and olive oil.
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then let her press and vomit in condensies, and tie up her mouth and nose for an hour;
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If it is now, the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands come out freely, then it is fitting to let them settle gradually one by one.
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter again, then put the woman on the bed, and lift up her feet.
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then throw the bed onto the ground, and secure the woman, so she does not fall when standing.
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot enter again, and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife which is there before mentioned, and extract the child, and set it aside in a proper manner.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child stands up on its feet, then they are fitting to push upwards.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn the wound a little by little, until it is even.
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then press against the pain and extend it a little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can he avoid the pain as soon as possible, if he commands so, and make him vomit with condensation;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he survives, God will be merciful.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not so as we have said, if the blood flows little by little, day by day, until it reaches its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if he does not come back as we have seen, said so take muscilynge of alum, and oil of chamomile, and gum pounded, and crush all in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put the ointment on the belly of the woman inside and cover that ointment, then make her sit in water until just below the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when she is softened because of it, he will make a girdle of iron around her, and put her down, and let one hour pass;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then he will set her on the bed, then he will open her and restrain her mouth and nose, and lightly press on her abdomen, because she now gasps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child after its birth on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the patient comes in this state, he will then put the bile on her hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	Then she will turn to her back on the bed, and let her feet hang down, and then lie still.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and then he will gently pull her hands up little by little, and then press on her hands above the belly, and take off the couch below, so that she is properly arranged.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the fever does not burst, take his feet and hold him firm, then move his feet up to his belly, then give him water.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and pull the child little by little;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to apply herself to the child until it breaks.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child that comes out wide with one hand only
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is advisable to engineer to return the hand;
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be returned, have the woman lift herself up and go.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, place her on the bed and make her feet move.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the medicinal herbs that I have mentioned;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if it is pregnant, then make her sit on the bed; then study how to bring back the hand.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and bring forth the child according to its natural shape; and make it cut out, and instruct her to bind herself until the swelling subsides.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child from his neck down to his arms, and had spread out his hands, and his face turned towards his back towards his mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is suitable that the surgeon hold his hand tight, then turn it slowly and slowly, and set her lightly.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is evened out, then put on the natural muscle oil of flesh and fat, as we have said; and instruct her to move slowly.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, make her sit on the bed; and instruct her to bind herself.
et la fai esternuer.	And cut off.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner to all the rest.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to this manner on the second joint, if you strike the second joint until the moistures are cleared;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if there is a fever on its face and on its neck, if you strike the throat, so that it does not stop, and the child dies;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then pour the child into the basin, until you have put it in as it is fit, and instruct the woman not to give it any medicine.
adonques si istra legierement.	and thus if it is lightly drawn.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that many times it will be born with a head, and sometimes without one.
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is no strange thing, and it has happened often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	They are strange things, and they do not live if it is named.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and they are caused to flourish by the flesh which devises them, which is connected to the blood;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and there is no time when they are not present naturally like all of us have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they are severe, then the cure is as we have said, and it is a subtle bile, and quickly and lightly what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and so quickly that they are worth more than usual to the health.
de plusors enfans	Many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Never are they formed in the first or second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, or more than fifteen, and all take on the shape of an infant by the measure of its size, glorious juice, because it is possible that such a thing may have happened;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	If it happens as they advise.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When treating a woman with child who has died or miscarried, as I have said in the previous division, and there is no fever, you must perform surgical work with your hands.
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	if it is fitting that you know whether the woman has good health, and has not had an accident or has fear of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	if it is fitting that the woman lies on her back with her knees bent and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister applies the ligature of the second part, or ties her to the bed so that she is not treated with the descent of the child.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oils using musk and fenugreek and sesame seeds, and then apply the balm to her hands with these oils and musk.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	Now let the wounds heal lightly; then you should pour wine into the marrow lightly, and later pour vinegar onto what is suitable for this, and take care that the fever does not appear upon his head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if he strikes the glands in his eyes or on his neck or in his mouth or under his tongue or behind his beard or under his chin or near the ribs, and if the ulcers are on his feet, strike them or prick them and cut the middle of the bones.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that the ulcer appears on his right hand, and place a poultice between the two fingers of his left hand, and pour wine all over his right hand, and strike the ulcer in any of those places that we have mentioned, until it comes to a clean opening.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the onion:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then strike into another onion, or if you need it, so that the extraction is even.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it evenly by moving from one side and the other, so that they come out, and so that the onions are cut to make them hold, as this is the shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if some part remains, then take some of its juice from one of its two sides, and pour it into that part, and treat the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if it does not remain at all, then put this onion a little higher, and do that until it is full of fire.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be returned by stretching, then you must wrap above the bandage, until it is all tight.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	Then take the axe in the joint of the foot or on the thigh, and do it in the other hand, and make it twice.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the head of the child is swollen and it has a large bone in the discharge or if he has a high fever with an assembled head, then you should pour the spindle-like brush between your two fingers, make the head and extract the fever.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you put it on the instrument called "almaid", because the form comes with the instruments or scalpel which is after this.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and do the same if the child has great natural fever;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then treat the bones with tongs, and if the joints burst, hold the joint with forceps, until the moisture which is or in the discharge is dried.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	And if she cannot come out, then cut her by pieces at the root where you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you should pierce it as long as the moistors come out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the patient is sitting on his feet, so that there is less pressure on the legs, and the direction of the stomach towards the mouth is lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is swollen in the stomach or intestines, then you must extract it above the groin on the leg.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and pull out the stomach or intestines, until they run out.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if other members are swollen and the joint is fixed, then pour the bile into his mouth by pouring from the navel.
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then pour one or two ounces, and bring forth.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the nose is compressed by an abscess cold that has come to it, so it should not be strained again, but rather administer soft and wet things.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and they must apply poultices, and slice in moist fleshy things and moisten.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child lies on its chest, and you can place it even, then administer those things that we have said for a living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one does not have power, then tie the wound to pieces, and leave nothing of the second line.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, administer those things that we have said regarding abscesses in the nose that come into it.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if they bleed excessively comes, so whether it is put into water, restrain, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom an infant was dead, and she sought another one above it, and then the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After many times the thing happened in the mouth, and it swelled so much that it burst, and great pain came.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was deceived; there is no translation to provide. The text appears to be incomplete or contains formatting issues. Please provide the rest of the text for me to translate.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed a splint of great attraction, and from it an os came out, after some other days.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed a great deal, because this has no bone in the belly.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I wanted to know the wound, and by probing with my hands, until the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman long time remained thus, and afterwards she died a little while later with pain in her bowels.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have only recorded this chapter because whenever the masters find an unusual thing, they seek assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	Let go of your hair to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Now comes the form of the pressure, for which we use books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and to both joints apply to both bones.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Everywhere, the nails should be more subtle in the restraint, and made of ivory or boxwood.
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And so the mouth of the fist is made very wide, and the margin of the tree is cut, and from long one palm and a half.
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And in the two limbs are two adjacent fist-like shapes, which are firmly fixed on one and the other, of a palm and half an inch or slightly more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	And these two adjacent shapes are bound in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form is made to resemble it even more subtly and lightly, of a beech or box wood fist, according to the likeness of the nails.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	And has both two fists two adjacent shapes, so as you see, of a palm and half an inch, and both twice as wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	And when you see to open a vein with all the instruments, then seat the woman upon a litter, and place her feet on both sides of it, and then pour two instruments together into the vein, and hold the head of the instrument between its handles.
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Then operate your hand over all the instruments, so that you have closed both jaws equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the vein of the arm, until it is made as tight as she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	This instrument is on top of them, and they are all multiplied in their appearances;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	And when the instruments have been prepared for them, it is even faster to operate, and they are higher in number according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you don’t see the instrument that is prepared in front of you, for it is not unnecessary.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the shoulder joint is retained in the child, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to grip his arm, and then have him exert himself on his back, and tie your hands to his mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she should fall through this, that is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this does not work, then cut the flesh, and make a puncture or wound, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the mare, such as camphor, anise, chamomile, safflower, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or none of them, be boiled or put in water on the fire.
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a caustic or burnt pot on one head and the other in the mouth of the mare, and tie it tight until the vapors come out from within the mare.
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the flesh, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If he has a broken bone immediately.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not improve as much, instruct the physician to pour oil of sesame or musk into his left hand, and then drink from its source, and want the second treatment.
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when it is found, grasp it and stretch it little by little straight away, so that the hairs do not break at the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but it is necessary to move it lightly from right to left and then treat.
si venra et se desaerdra.	if it comes and falls apart.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the hair of the marrow is tightly closed, we have already said the treatment of removing and fumigating with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	And if it is not what we have said, so beware that you do not go mad while treating.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is true that what is at the mouth of the mare, which you tie to the chest of the woman, then bind with linen thread.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	so that if the poultice is applied and it comes, and arrives.
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but beware, when you apply it, because if she vomits so that the bad smell comes to her stomach and head, and sickens the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	so then it is necessary to apply fumigation, which is a common remedy for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	no one of the ancients has tried fumigation with crescent and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which to fumigate a woman, when it is held by the flowers and second joint if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to look like an ape, and put the head subtle in its place, and bind the arms wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let there be fumigation over the embers, and the itch till it is spent, and begin again.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Most children are born without any solid foundation, whereas the head is inflated by some subtle humors.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is necessary to balance when the humors are inflating because of its swelling, and not pour a bad quality into it, but rather tighten the bandage so that it does not touch.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put a wet linen on it in wine and oil, and apply the dressing until he is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt whether it will stop bleeding, then tie off a vein with a tourniquet and let the hands rest for a while, and put on an ostomy when the child gets up to go to bed in the room.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes comes this sudden collapse of a wound or an abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	then it is necessary to cover that wound.
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if you have been cured, as we have said about the sharp iron cut.
de la fistule dou fondement	of a fistula on the underlying part
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Ulcers that come from under the foundation are nodulations, and swelling that comes from over the foundation or in the space between the two parts, if there is an ulcer or more.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that nodulation is old, it becomes inflamed, and moistens the whitish or subtle bowel, and sometimes these ulcers are painful.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and are considered to be caused by what is ejected or ventousity because the patient ejects, and sometimes in an attempt at it.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	If there are fistulas that have perforated the bladder, and just above the middle of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and come to just above the hip joint and just outside of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And so finds one that persists to the foundation, and not persisting:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you pour your dirty index or foundation, and pour a subtle needle of iron or thread into the fistula when there is no twistiness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twistiness, then you pour a subtle tentacle or the horsehair, until you feel the tentacle or the hair at your mouth.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there comes a purging of stool or vomiting or fever, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	She does not prick.
si te haste dou curer.	If you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is passed just to the bladder or just to the channel of the urine, then it falls into the urine, and cannot be fixed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	But if she pricks right at the joint of the elbow, if the pain comes again to the left.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	but if there is no twisting and the hurt cannot be removed by treatment or with ointment.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these Persian fistulas, there is no cure but hard work and the vanity of foolish people who get involved.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In that which is neither Persian nor ancient, there is hope of health by iron, as I have proved, and if the sick patient lies between your hands on his back.
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And lift the legs up to their knees, and let the knees be inclined towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then pour out some tar or pitch into the wound, or if it has tortuosity, until you see where the opening comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels pain in the bottom part, if so then pour out your two indices, since then you see if the opening has pierced.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	And whether it is discovered or you feel between your thumb the sinus or the cartilage, then know that it is a puncture.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If it cannot be pulled out, neither can it be saved.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	But there is one who is able to heal all cases, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And so instruct the assistant to make it happen, for when it is done as was said before, if you shave the cauterized area according to its size, just like he said;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and pourge the whole inside of the fistula, till it comes from the foundation;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this twice or three times, till you know that these burns should be applied, which are resembling to a feather of a bird;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then apply a moist poultice in butter, till the burns are healed, and then apply a dressing of lint and stitching.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he has such a sickness, this is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	For if this, there is no other way to be cured;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if they pierce between them, and not exactly at the point where it is on the foundation, and between your thumb and the tent, there is a thick covering of fat or flesh, and you see the fistula heal with this covering soft as wool;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If they prick at the beginning of the ulcer, and drink blood afterwards before the tenting, and then apply the cautery, until it comes to a head in the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the head of the ulcer will be discharged and will fall out;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and then make a demonstration of those charred things that seem like a goose feather, and there will be nothing left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not want you to cut between yourself and the wound, but cuts in place of you, whether with fire or with a cooling medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cautery has two effects:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	which is to say, the inflammation of those charred things, and the contraction of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	and then the cure for moist tents in butter or in hoarfrost, until it is dried out and the head of the charred thing falls into the bowel.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Now cure the wound of quick-healing bandages which are tied tight with a harsh thread, and these drying medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes just to the bottom of its foundation and is distant from the body, then put two or three pounds into its center and inquire.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the pain and enter through two openings where it is like piercing, or if there is only fire on the way of hope and expectation, through the administration of one of three kinds.
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cautersize as we have said, or you cut just to the root, or if you can, take out needles and treat as first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far into the root, lest you cover the foundation that holds it in place, and the excretions come out in an unintended direction.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	In case of good health, or if you should lose the covering and the wound then when it is struck at the foundation, or by attempt or by another instrument pointed out;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	and then you must define that free thing which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	and then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the opposite part from the foundation;
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if you give a lighter thing to the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	and no fistulas occur in this way;
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is coming out near the foundation of the skin above, if you take a tent which looks like this at the head;
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I cut the thread on one side and put a tent all along the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	She is pierced on the margin of the foundation within, then extract the finger from that puncture, as you pour your dough or foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	And tie the head of the finger together, and assemble both joints together, and hold one to the other, and let it rest for one day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	And hold him tight at all times, until the fingers have closed up these spaces that are between them;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then treat the wound till it is sound and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If they have a fistula or abscess, so pierce it in every manner that you can, if it's not too deeply penetrated.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to tie with a cover if it's too deeply penetrated, and then treat it, as we have said, until it's safe.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spiny staff which we make a fistula from is very rough with one and a half fingers and sharp points;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	And on the other hand not, because of that one does not strike what they should not strike, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Bloodletting can be done in two ways:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	Where they are in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and if there are small and large ones, cut to open the wound, and if there is one or more, remove them from the foundation and the head of the foundation.
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are removed do not have much moisture, and cut to open one or a little of the juice of citron or blood, and they have a red color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those who have them in the foundation, so that you instruct the patient to cough towards the chambers, until the foundations become firm, and they appear the threads.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if it comes to hand, and you pierce with nails, or hold it with your finger, then cut in its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if they cannot hold their wound shut by its moisture, then take it to the linen cloth or cotton, or from a piece of camel skin;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and cut it open on both sides, then cut, and powder over it with some hot powders that will replace the cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you will cauterize as it is said in the chapter of cautery, for the cures of other cures until they are healed;
