et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the fundament cannot come out, then bandage the patient with a strong and bitter cloth to cleanse what is in the fundament, if it can come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient is in pain, and if the child has a hard fundament, then the treatment is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and so you must grasp at your joint or with tongs, and strike, then heal as we have said, until it is sound, and that the fear of incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	if it seems fitting to dress the wound in this way:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	take a thread of the right kind, and put it in an awl, and then draw the thread above and pierce the awl on the other side, and twist the two threads with the awl below, and if so, make them tight.
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and tighten the thread firmly, then take it away, and extract the awl, and do so for all the others, and leave one for draining out the superfluity of the wound;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a moist cloth in rose oil or in ceruse, and put it on the wound, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then let him stand for a while, so that he passes, and when he is cut, so that the treatment of ointment and other treatments are performed until he becomes whole.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when cutting firmly with a knife or fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It happens frequently when there is a sharp pain in the intestine, and by the force of nature, and because the illness is old and medicine is useless.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is fitting to reset him at the point of a spatula or with your nail to remove the scab above, which does not allow it to moisten;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat him until he is whole, as he should.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot be healed, then reapply the rasping more forcefully than before, until he becomes whole and is scabbed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him until he is whole.
dou fremit	do the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A rash is an unintended appearance on the body, and it will go through its full course;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes the blood freezes, and it feels like death is coming, and it comes to all parts of the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane of a goose quill or a strong vulture's feather, and put that cane on the freezing blood, until the purple circles appear all over it.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand to the entire cane until you cut all over the freezing blood, and put it into its very roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if it is a thorn of thistle or iron, do so with a thorn from the same material and in that shape, being subtle under and above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Don't pierce, for this will hold them together, and press.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, cauterize the freezing blood, just as it is in front of or near the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of a hollow castor bean.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Nothing is done with gold or lead, or melted tin, or cloth.
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	And never is anything done with these small and large instruments, according to what they are suitable for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These are therefore the instruments used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the needle small and large when it is used large, or if the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	And if there is a defecation or the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is inside perceived.
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	And if it has a hollow on one side and an opening on the other;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And if the belly or an animal (is treated) with medicines from a cow's bladder or parchment; and if there is perceived all of those small holes, and between each hole there must be space, then fill in one of them with thread very tightly wound around X (or whatever), and sew up the belly like a sow.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	And when the medicine is present, so hold it in front of an instrument made of a strong thread, then bind.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and oil the head with a binding of oil or lard or beeswax, or something similar, then pour it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the physician makes his fingers bind him with both hands together, until he is completely still, then remove the binding, and lift up the patient's legs to show, and if the medicine comes out, tie him as much as possible.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night in this manner, it is more great aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you bind the boils in a disease of decayed belly, and the medicine comes out quickly, so that it recurs when he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if they bleed out from their root or abscess, whether it is a cyst as subtle as for an infant;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle cyst where the skin is constricted:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already discussed in dividing how to treat wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or you will say the remedies for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to which part or place the wounds are located, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	Things are made so that wounds are caused by a blow of stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or lance, or stick, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that they are made according to the laws of the body, as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or flesh, or belly, or liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and start with simple head wounds, because they remember coming in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	When a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is due to stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn apart and the wound is great, and you are slightly afraid of an abscess.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if you treat the head wound immediately, if it comes from bleeding of the wound, and treat one side against the other side of the belly.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and the patients should be replenished with wine and thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not recover, if he is weakened by thin food, and does not drink wine, and does not eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put salve on the wound, if an abscess forms there, cotton wool soaked in rose oil alone, or vinegar suppository.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if it is not an abscess there, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and does not move from the air, powder, I will say one of these below.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the blood has moved it, then put on some ointments until it is clean.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by stitches, then assemble them by suturing, as I will say about wounds in the belly, of the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to bone and skin, and sticks only at one point, cut.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine, and restore the flesh by replacing it with leather, and instruct the patient to eat large quantities of food, such as meat, cooked eggs, and poultry, as well as similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	If you find rot or putrefaction, and it has not reached the bone, cut it through completely, and throw away, then take care.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	If there is an artery in the wound or vein, without applying a tourniquet, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, choose to release the artery, and if you find the artery is loosened, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If this does not benefit, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light.
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and that you apply this powder which causes the pain to move.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	Take some embers (fire) part from them;
sanc de dragon II parties;	blood of the dragon two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Mix three parts of vivifying powder and subtle powder, apply to the wound, bind and fasten so that it bleeds well and unites with its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then tie well, and let loose when it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for you do not remove the medicine until she is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made alone with calcined vivae, when you do not have cense or blood of dragon, but the artery has been moved by the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	and if the artery moves the wound itself, at that very moment, do not put on this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put some digestive ointments or powder made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until it sets well;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	the healer of other remedies until he is cured.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	and if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, so that the strait is pinched finely;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about this later after the head fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between the one on the head and the other, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	if it is the neck, if there is no other remedy to leave the treatment and put nothing restraining, for he heals slowly and makes them retreat;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of the sickness is with the brain, which is in the higher members;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but if medicine is needed, such as calcining in sweet water and mixing with rose oil, and cooling the solution also in sweet water, and other minerals like this, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so that the skin and tendons are cut and bound with bandages, then the treatment continues until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and he has a head full of blood, then cut to the lower part.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the arteries are cut open and bleeding comes, then take out the artery, and apply ointment, and cautery to cauterize it.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spines of the throat are cut open or the nerves, and the vessels are bound up because the flesh is going, then cut the vein on the chain of the neck, but do not touch the throat itself, rather apply it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind him at once, and let him stay for some days, then the treatment of ointments and poultices until he is made whole.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has caused impression in the bone;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if he has broken bones, so that the limbs are completely frozen and unable to move, and whatever you can't see, leave until the wound is closed and the limb is set straight again.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, so powder on top of the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has an abscess, then the treatment will be as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of arrow or sword wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it's an arrowhead or a knife cut, and the wound is deep, then look at how many arrows have gone through to see if the patient will live.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	so you know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it's not deep, and the wound is fresh all over with its blood, then don't put powder on it for the first hour, nor tie it to prevent the bleeding as much as possible, revive him in your arms, and give medicine to the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But I apply an attractive dressing twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	And if you do not have dressing, put cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four days, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	But if there is no spasm, nor trembling of the heart, due to an evil spirit.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see the healthy disposition, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it then with poultices and other remedies, until it is fully healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	And if it cannot heal and close, then know that there is an abscess;
si la cure si com on doit.	If the cure is as we must.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision with a sword or a knife, and it's shallow, or deep, or on the back, then do the cure of what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	since she is great, stitch it up.
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it's small, cover it with powder; and if it's pierced into the bone, and has cut off pieces, as it pleases, and if they are exposed wounds.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if there aren't exposed wounds, then leave the wound to dry out, for it will ease the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds that affect other members, consider the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	a rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The internal rupture of the intestines is great and painful;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	when there is a large wound in which no intestine can pass, or the intestines themselves are torn apart, because of the infection.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitches are more painful, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because of this we put in more stitches to close the intestines, when not putting them back inside their original position.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestine swells so quickly that it feels the pain, if it is put back in stitches again, and because of this small wounds are more painful, so that one must clean these internal injuries like others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And says that the intestinal rupture is in four kinds:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The common stitches that occur on the belly, and the stitches for other wounds of the body, are also common with other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all those stitches are more proper with the belly stitch, and I will tell you each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I said that when the wound is small, and no intestine has been ruptured, and there is little to put back together, it is one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we said, or because the intestine is swollen from the blow.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, burn him in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Molest him with an onion soaked in hot water or with a handful of cloth dipped in cold water, until the swelling is gone.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this wine is made to restrain, and it causes the soul to shrink.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with water or make it high and boil, because by this is cleared the entry into little things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then they make the wound slightly larger with that tool on which the hemorrhoids are struck;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is that they shrink it to its size, so that none of us should cut it unless there is great need.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the way to break it;
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so they cut inside the hornet's nest and do not retreat, and see how the form is.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines spring out, if you put it back in its own natural form according to its own place, if you have the power, because this is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, it is fitting that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you put his head and belly higher than the lower parts, and also if there is a rupture of the belly in one of its two parts, so that the navel is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and accordingly it is fitting to do as I said in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds put on what is suitable, and then hold in your hands the minister who holds all the wound in his hand, and assemble the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common method of stitches, and it is that you prick an arrow or more, according to the quantity of the wound's width; then let one inch from the top of the wound, and poke in with a needle or strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	And pierce the two sinew tendons with two needle tendons, which are inside the skin, until you pierce from that part; then assemble the two head of needles four together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then thread the end of a double thread around the needle in two parts; then assemble the two head of stitches on the wound together, and let one inch from that point, and poke in with another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread in the same way you made the first needle, and do not stop doing that until all the wound is held tight;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium in size, between fine and coarse, for the fine needles pierce all of the flesh, and the too large ones cannot enter very well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this is why they must be medium in size.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not wise to push the needles too far into the flesh and the skin, lest they pierce and open up the wound before the suturing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut the needles to stop the bleeding of the patient while they sleep, and put tourniquets or bandages around the points of the needles to keep them from pulsing, and let them stay there until the wound is sutured.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of suturing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because it uses either one needle.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second operation is common, and it is that you assemble the two head of the skin and the two joints of the flesh together with an awl or with one strong thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have assembled the two heads of the skin four times, then take out the awl from where you started, in the way one cuts threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each seam the thickness of a small penny;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This costure takes seven hours, and I sewed a wound on one man who had an arrow wound in his belly, which was pierced by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm of flesh, and it was the intestines well two palms of flesh, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I let my intestine alone for 24 hours then it stopped bleeding after 15 days, and the cure, and was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they had taken him to judgment that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not treat him with medicine, because I was in the left place where there is no remedy or medicine to be found;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put more wool on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	or I will tell you two proper ways to sew:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and thread from that same place inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when she has pierced the correct mark from straight to straight, whether it is on the skin of a siphon or on a cut or wherever you have sewn the needle, and then pierce her from that same place inside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	For the ears of this costume, so that you sew as the barber does the hair, and you leave once the incision is made on one side, and the other covers it, until the costume is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of costume, which the Galens call properly, is this: they put together both parts in one piece naturally, and join one part of the skin to another part of the skin, like so:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Stick a needle or a small pin close to the wound, and pierce it alone, and leave both joints of the skin.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and pierce it from the opposite side inside, through both joints of the skin.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce one of each from the back part which was previously hidden in that place, in two other joints on the opposite side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common method of sewing and stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	People who are not familiar with this phrase, and none of them testify to it, we must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in one.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and you must put one needle from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew open wounds.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and it is known that when a rupture occurs in the belly, the stitching is more grievous than for other wounds on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, in such a way that the arrow has moved it, then you put back the intestine and the cost.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder mixed with charcoal, and if the arrow has moved it, put on any dressing that is available, until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut off the thread, and sew the sinew, and the mirror;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as you do with others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you do not have medicine, put on, immediately until it comes out to the surface, cotton wool, and move it two times a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	You have no need for any other medicine apart from simple cases.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will not cause commonality to the principal members, then it is recommended that you make a lighter application of oil on olive tree warm, or rose oil, and put it between the angles, and under the awnings;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and it often happens, if you give him black vinegar clisters, and most of the time the putrefaction comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and drill inside, and see that when it's the large intestine, it's easier to cure than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "youth" cannot heal when it is diseased, and this is because of the coldness of the veins, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach of its nature towards death.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the zirb jumps out of the wound, then set it back as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it has grown old and become black like that, then it is proper to cut the limb which has turned black, lest blood does not come out of it again, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then tie what is between the ligature, and hang the two heads down from the lower part of the wound to relieve the extraction of the serpents that come out, and the wounds.
de la routure dou boueil	of the burn from a hot iron.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are swollen, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I have seen that one man was crippled or had his belly torn by a lance.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and this was the wound in the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into an abscess, and from that came the expulsion and the vomiting.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I will translate the text line by line into English.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him heal, I doubted that the patient had a bad condition in his stomach.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no illness, but remained in better conditions, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimented that when he had a small wound in the intestine, he should be bound in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	wrap the gauze around great testicles, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the gauze has closed over the mouth, place it on both lips, so that it chokes his mouth.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then he strikes the testicles, and this holds so that he cannot loosen it, then puts another gauze on in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely closed.
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	When the intestines are bound with a thread in the intestine of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this thread from the intestine that is very clean, and then tie to the head of the other fine thread twisted with linen, and push the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it through the route.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this method of sewing is not effective except according to the way of promise and expectation;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal channels, then there will be no gain or healing except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or however it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	That which has grown long, when it begins to wither, is called a fistula; and even when it is swollen and has turned into an abscess.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the shape of the node that is not free and hard and white, or one does not feel pain, and is also like the beak of a bird's feather;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	none of the above, or somewhat.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about the division of wounds in my previous writings, that any wound which is not healed, and does not have ulcers, is only caused by one of the seven reasons:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, from the smallness of the wound or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its malevolence;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has hard flesh inside and on the lips, which prevents ulcers from forming;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	There is too much blood;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the meat is spoiled and of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or if the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because of that, corruption is a kind of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because in the region's property, digestion is late, health is also late, and escapes by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have shown all these causes, and signs, and treatments of medicine in the cutting.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I inform you about the treatment of fistulas, which are created by hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Observing that a fistula has occurred in every member of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For in the fistulas that come from great veins, and from arteries, and from nerves, or to the scrotum, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or on some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to damage of the principal member, and like this.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas of this manner are a hindrance to healing, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no fistula that has not come to you just like I said, and you have taken it for a cure, and it seems to be working, then take a tent of iron or wire, whether the fistula is straight, or crooked.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the abscess is twisted, then search for a subtle attempt to insert it deeper, because the points bend and move into the twisting.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the abscess has broken through and you cannot see it well by searching with attempts, then try to isolate it by one of the breaks, because the moisture is short from one break and contaminates;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and then ask for a careful examination of your poor body, so you know if it has bones or nerves, and see whether the bone is exposed to the fullest, and ask the patient well where he feels the pain when I press with my hand;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know where it is, and if it is near a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and extract the worst part and the rotten flesh that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then the treatment as long as it is safe, and if the fistula is well set in straight, so that you can copy them by depth, as long as you are able, then put wet towels on medicine cold, and pour juice into the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the remaining surplus at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put salve in equal proportions to keep it healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not kept healthy by this, then the cautery as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then make a copy.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If you wish or nurse them do not trouble or main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then keep it until the corruption is completely gone, then do treatment in equal proportions as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not well, and the bow breaks like before, know that you are not far from death.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it is discovered and you want to be at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore life;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is so well, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	But if not, know that the corruption is too far gone, and you cannot recover;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	unless there's no other remedy but to put your life in nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there's only a small corrupted bone, and you can treat it with tongs, if the instrument is suitable for it, and if it has many bones, then do not leave one behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture causes it to turn against him, and there is no mistake or fear, then he will be struck by both moisture and cold, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove it in an hour, place the wound covered with a poultice to prevent putrefaction, and let them remain until the flesh is decayed between the bones, then they will have less difficulty with the bones.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as the thigh or knee, then only repair the decay until all the marrow has gone, and then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of the corruption, and it brings just to the bone.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it is best to cover and cover all just until the point of the corruption, and then treat the patient until they are well.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to someone at home in their leg, so that you may take an example and help with your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man in his XXX years who had pain in his leg due to something that came from within the body, until the matter came out through his leg, and a large abscess broke open, and he could not get rid of it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the physician by his folly operated above so that the abscesses opened up and a lot of matter came out, and it became a fistula, and it was very painful to everyone who felt it in their body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And many physicians had operated on him for two years without any success in the art of hands, until I was called and came to see his leg and the remedies that were being used to cure it, and what was coming out through the boils was causing great pain.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And it would become red the body of the young man, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I applied a poultice to one of the boils, and then I searched for all the boils, and found that some came together from different parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I failed then, and cut into one of the wounds so that I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, with corruption inside the bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I recognized what appeared to be the rotten bone, and thought that there could be no other corruption, except for the one I had taken.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medicinal salts over a long period of time and could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then resumed, and discovered the bone in its original form, and found that the corruption was still present in the bone, and I thought about sewing it back together.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But I could not bear to cut into one palm of bone, and the wound became all swollen, then I restored it with medicine.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and the swelling went away quickly, and I did not want to reopen the wound further except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and because of my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood so often occurs, but it has healed completely, and in its place an hard char came out of the bone, and was of good disposition and had no harm or counter-evil in all things, neither at the bedside nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be set in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	bind it tight, and stretch the ligature to the top of the bone that is open.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and I put another stronger rope around the first one, and bind it above the joint that has opened the bone, and stretch it there, if you treat the corrupt part downwards, uncover the healthy part above, where it is visible, until the sinew does not bleed the healthy part.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And let him tie it to a stick or a table below the bone so he covers the corrupted flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to cover it as often as one can see and feel the corruption, and cover again afterwards.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	But if the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then he must cut away the flesh entirely.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then let him tie sticks underneath, and then cover the corruption with one part over another; cover it so that the upper part is close to but not on top of the corruption as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then he must cut the corrupted joint, and cover the bone where it contains corruption on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is at the continuation of both joints, there is no other source than from the covering;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the corruption is in a finger of the hand, or in a finger of the foot, it is very severe in that case, but nonetheless you must inquire about the source of that corruption, how it arose;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways you can, but so that the vein or the nerve does not prevent you from doing so;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisors and the hairs around these bones are many, according to the base of the bone and its appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and fragility, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each similar form with its own instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And you will know from the work that it will show you the instrument which you have need of, according to your knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways in which the diseases are treated;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think the instrument that you have need of according to what it is suited for.
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	the joints are supposed to be moved either due to something being inside, or due to something being lacking;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have medicine to heal the corruption by the treatment of medicines, and it does not help, if it is necessary to cover that limb up to its root where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes either by death or by the evil of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the limbs become black, as if they were burnt with fire, and afterward pus forms, which goes to each limb in succession, and spreads throughout the body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you have haste to cover yourself, and if it is by the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as scorpions from the sea and wyrms and similar ones, if the wound is on the head with two cuts, if they strike, and give no space between coming just to your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes just to the hand, if it strikes the joint, so that the wound does not come to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, if it strikes the bone;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the bone, it is death, and there are no medicinal fires worth anything except the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and thus you must do so whenever the wound comes to the bone:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes to the first joint, then she must strike after the second joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes upon a bone, then cut the entire bone.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if she rises on the leg, then strike at the joint of the knee.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if she comes above the knee, then there is no other action but to strangle the patient to death.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sewing the member if it is that you tie it above and below, and stretch out one strap below and another above, and serve the flesh between the two straps to a width of one span, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or sew, and put a strip of linen on each side, so that the seam does not touch the healthy part, and it comes to the patient another wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	If blood comes out when you cut, then cauterize the wound immediately, or apply some powders that restrain it;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is complete, and bind the injured limb with a strong bandage, and cure it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you how it happened in the house when it was under siege;
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	there happened a blackness that seemed like fire, and this corruption came first to his two feet, until it consumed the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when he saw the corruption, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after that, the corruption returned to his two hands, and he came to me, and I put certain remedies on him after purifying his body, but it could not be stopped.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And I command you to cut open my hand, and I do not wish that I have hope of feeling the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also fear that if my hand is cut open, he will die, for the virtues of the flesh are weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he was desperate and returned to his land, and sought to cover his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have this story told only because of the fact that someone needs to do it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No time ever comes when an abscess appears on the jaw, and lingers for so long that it causes a great swelling of the face.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it rots and infects, and the swelling goes away, just like in our own bodies.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin that is above is as subtle as I weave, and it does not run against the bone, or against the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy", and it is not called "furuncle";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes against the bone to its full extent, then it is called "furuncle";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is that you cut through the entire skin, and at the same time when it is subtle, as we weave;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have taken a vow that the skin heals, and there is no corruption in its entirety, and the skin is thick with fat, then the surgeon should make an incision like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look to see if the breasts are large, and the bowels which are in them are of foul odor, then apply the Egyptian medicine that is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take onyx, and oil, and lard, equally, and put them to boil in one vessel over the fire, until the medicine becomes red, and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take as much of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and make a plaster for the breast, and tie up the hernia;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for two hours, then extract it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times until the breasts are well done, and come out loose.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And sometimes it clisters over water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from the vine's stock, and pour water above, then it flows out, and clisters, until you know that the breasts are well healed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	But if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then if you mix water and honey, so that there is a little lead in it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you mix it with honey and wine mead, so that the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine is made to warm the healthy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breasts are well purified, if the clisterization of what is born from the chyme in them, and if you make emplasture diaphanite, and do it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	If you prick at your base with these cautery tools, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the hole in the breast is small, and the needle of the cautery cannot enter, cut through with a small iron bar and apply an Egyptian bandage or basilicon cloth until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too large, so that only the cut or the cautery can enter it, and if a perforated bowels are above, cut through below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in its deepest passage, do not let it be released.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the breast beneath as it is seen, so that the bowel moves to its lowest passage, for when the bowel reaches its deepest point, do not let it be released, and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as it is seen, do so in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	The bowel moves lighter than expected and does not stop anything of the bowel.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take conservative medicines to place on the healthy part, and cover it with linen cloth that covers the entire body.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then tie the force to the broken breastbone in a way that is larger than the first one, for they apply ointment on the other covering according to the quantity of the break, and put it over the healthy part to alleviate the bowel, and do not hold back the large cloth with fire until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And he who is on the broken breastbone often opens the bowel, and knows whether it is poisoned or not, how much blood comes out, whether it is venomous or not, or if it is being digested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	And take care if the patient feels pain or distress, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has reached this degree of spread and you see the nature that lies above the hurt flesh, then learn that the limbs are ailing.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then release the bandage in the morning or on the third day, and when you open the wound, change another dressing, and renew the wrapping.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast moves back and forth indigestion after many days, you see that the breasts do not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the fine veins are cut after long time, do not despair of your health, for good health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are some who delay treating their wounds with charcoal, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if he has an indigestion that causes pain in the breast after many days, learn that the breasts are not healing.

puis le confit et en use;	then the dressing is applied afterwards;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and the same thing is done as a confection, when it is not present at the wound, or you take a mirror and oil and incense, and break them, and grind the powder on the honey when it is on the fire;

et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and using simple or compound remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Break the bone, and make a powder, and put on the honey that I said, and apply it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the patient is long-lived and has not been cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has gone to the very bone, or is causing hardness in the bones, or swelling.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	as for the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	From the root of the abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that forms in the space between the thumb and the palm of the hand, or in the toe, or sometimes elsewhere.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is old and no one takes care of it, the abscess can come to the toe, and it spreads and fills with pus as much as possible, until it reaches the root of the ulcer, and sometimes even further.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion just to the bone, until it comes with painful odor, and the joints become swollen, and the color flees.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we said in the division, and the cure does not work at all, then it is necessary to copy on it; that is, to make a piece of the flesh around the abscess until its remaining part is closed up, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is much great aid if the bone is sound and the joint is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the joint presses on the cartilage and begins to pierce it, and the flesh bleeds, so that you must put on the right under the joint, pointing towards the cartilage, and the nail in above, and strike that subtle and light blow, and put on the rest of the cartilage with medicines burning and corrosive to remove.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure shall be applied until it is sound.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then strike it, and pull out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, so will not heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the wounds corrupting, then treat them in the way as it has been said, until they are cured.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if he is frozen and swollen, and feels great pain, it is best that you cure him first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the swollen area with a sharp instrument, cutting across it, and be careful that the incision does not go too close to the flesh beneath the swelling, because the patient will feel great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is anything put on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain comes from a swollen finger.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The swollen joints of those who have been injured by the blows of others' hands sometimes burst, and sometimes there are bones, and at times a single joint, and never does any birth occur in the roots of the joints, or they do not come out from some bone.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born with no sign of the wound do not move at all, and those who are born at the joint of the wound may or may not move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The height of him who is fat is lighter, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	height measured from the root of a broad spatumile.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born at the root of a joint is injured to be cured:
si te tien dou coper.	if he holds himself tight.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born or must be at the rear end, if it is fitting that you copy the circular movement just over the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate needle to its suitable length, and cure until he is well.
