Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden sounds that come from within the joint occur by birth, or by a sudden wound, or by fire's burning, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If one covers that wound, so the broken part must be repaired according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then puts between two towels or cloths moistened in rose oil, so they will not stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin strips of ponce (a type of fabric), until they stick, if it is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the sound comes to one of his two joints with the palm, cut the wound as it seems fitting.
des vils	The old ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	These are heavy veins swollen with a foul pus, full of melancholy humors, which come out in more severe members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it happens most to those who walk on feet and work hard and carry burdens.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary to give them no stomach medicine and then cleanse with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	There are two ways of treating with iron.
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is to cut them open and treat the black wound;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is to tie off the vein and drain its force.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is according to this method;
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	the first is the ankle of a hot water vessel very strong, until the thick flesh is broken down, then strain the swollen leg of the sick person from above to below at the level of the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Now cut the vein at the joint, whether it's in the left or right hand, of a large size, then raise and pull out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much as possible without causing harm to the patient.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it, and instruct him to fasten his diet eating black meat.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the evacuation and bleeding when veins are empty, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The bloodletting is done in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	raise the leg of the patient, if it has much hair, then put it in hot water, and let the leg be immersed in warm water until it becomes red, and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have pain, then apply the heat of fire, and then strike it directly into the vein at the long distance to the head at the side of the knee; or in the lower part near the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then cover the wound with linen, and burn the vein from each side until it stops bleeding when felt;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and then you see the vein red and black, and when it enters the linen so that it seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then pour out the blood below, until it is lifted up by the linen, and then put it on a lighter linen, then strike again into the other place, at the three-dozen.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then burn the skin above the vein until it stops bleeding, then lift it up by the blood, just as you have done, and put it on another linen, just as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Now I have to move another joint, or if you don't need more, then lift it and strike at the same height twice with two feet;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then pull out the joint by joint until it moves entirely, then strike.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot pull and lift it, then prick with a needle into the strong thread tightly fastened, strike, and turn your hand on both sides until it moves.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and hold that it will not strike again, because if it strikes, then it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it will cause harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have entirely pulled it out, put a linen cloth moistened in wine and oil on the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the healer so that he may be healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the body is broken and twisted and turned around together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must break it severely, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and cut it as we have previously instructed.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	the form of the bone from which one cuts the skull should be curved, and do not pierce it, lest you cut the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of large curvature, because if it were subtle, you would cut the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the lower limbs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in earth that has no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and perhaps it appears in another place than in the joints, and this happens due to putrefaction that comes from beneath the skin, as when it comes within the body like a snake and towards the flesh, you must press between the skin and the bone.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	If the inflammation of the vein is such that it comes to the leg a great swelling, then change the fluid, and begin the venesection forthwith, as one would take root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the joint is opened, it is advisable that you wrap around a piece of linen, one and a half fingers' breadth from the wrist to two and a half fingers' breadth, and the knee, and let the linen remain on the leg, and every time when it is not in front, wrap around the skin.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining part around, and do not cover its root, until all of it has been used up.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it off, it may return into the bone, and cause an abscess and putrefaction at that place, and a worse illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this small thing it is necessary to treat her little by little until the head, and there remains nothing in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And there is no time when this vein is treated with the length of one palm, or X, and someone comes to me who has come from X palms in length, and when you copy it, if it brings forth blood or is lost, and the arrow goes straight to the bone, so that all falls.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And if the material is empty inside, and nourishes with medicine for a day, then the cure does as the abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And there is no time when this vein bursts in the joint of the foot, or of the foot, and it comes out much blood, and from it come clots.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure the wound as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between the leather and the cartilage.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called "bovine malady" in our land, because it often affects those who have eaten beef, and it is a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, and moves up and down the entire body, causing pain from member to member, until the skin bursts or it jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is associated with the accumulation of some humors, such as worms, lice, and parasites that live in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its malevolence, because when it moves through the body, and goes up to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and cured, if it does not burn then, only.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	So it is necessary that you tie the patient above and below with a strong band tightly bound, then strike above and cure it, and if they fall to the bone completely in the chest, do not touch them, when burning with fire on top, until death occurs;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that they run on oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the oil, then bind under it the cord tightly formed, then strike above and cure.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to treat the patient with mundification of the body, using soluble medicines for corrupting humors, and if they are sick of spoiled or rotting flesh.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of pain which comes from inflammation
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I went to see a sick woman, and she showed me one of her arms, and saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and after that, I saw it growing even faster like a worm on the shoulder, much sooner than anything else, like living silver when it cuts through its flesh at another place.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain left the arm and went to the shoulder, and then it spread throughout the body for a little while, until it reached the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	The patient told me that they are turning inside out, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed greatly how she moved from one member to another, because I had never seen this disease in that way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	All the time I have heard that people who have had an operation like this are in great pain afterward, but I myself was not, just as I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that this was why the woman had a pale complexion and swelling of the veins, and because she appeared so constrained.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not appear like this because of that reason in those who are lean and have pale complexions and swollen veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see someone treating this illness, and the patient feels that pain, just as we have said, if they lift up and lower down hastily, and then strike them severely so that the swelling in the limb increases.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the joint;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it in your eyes, the physician of those who suffer from wind colic, as it is said to be caused by foul pills and serpent pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	due to arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their shapes and according to the sizes of their bodies or where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	For the diversity of them is that there are those with great points, and small ones, and spines, and sutures;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two points, and those with tongues, and those with pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those that shed into any member according to its two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member it sheds like cerebrum, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls down then in any limb of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary that you separate from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in various conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when that bad sign does not appear to you and the arrow is not driven straight into it, then you must take up a knife and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces the bone and passes through the brain, where scotoma and pain are felt, with redness on the eye, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and mixture of understanding, and vomiting blood.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And if by chance he does not have fever of the nose, or of the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and if by chance it affects his speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and falls out of the moist white wound like pus, and also as if it were burnt charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then take away the wound if it is not bound.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the wound when it bleeds or pus, is that it is near the left breast, and feels like if it were pierced in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and if the wound goes mute like pus, and in a black poultice, it comes with coldness and sweat, and fainting;
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	When they are old enough to sense doubt, then death comes.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never bears pain beyond a smooth discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, sighs high and breathes cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if an arrow shatters in the cover of the thigh, so that it is loose from the small bones.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and great sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow is shot into or through the stomach, by chance, it may jump out of the wound without removing any indigestible matter.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow shoots into or through the intestines and does not break up against the gallbladder, nor goes into any other part of the intestine, there is no hope for a good cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if an arrow shatters in the bladder, and the urine bursts forth and comes out, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Therefore he knows that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arm and shoulder and neck and elbow and shoulder joint and shoulder blade and spine of the back and fist and chest and arms and legs, are safe in proportion to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it's not venomous, just as I told you, because of this that you will do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It has happened in one’s home where an arrow pierced or cut the root of the nose;
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I pulled out from the other side the fat of the ear, and he was made whole in a short while.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And he pulled out a arrow from the fat of his ear under the parchment, and the arrow was returned, and you could only reach as far as the point towards his fist, and it was a large Turkish bow with all its iron near the ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The wound healed, and no other bad accident happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic bow.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beard, and worked on it very subtly until I pulled it out, and the Christian was made whole.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And carry a sash to the house where he was laid or on his belly, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed XXX days, if his condition did not improve.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut open the sash and tied it in place, and applied it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if I saw a man who had cut or bruised himself on his back.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the sash remained inside him for a while, and his natural disposition did not worsen, nor did he find any pain in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And saw another man who had cut an artery on his face, and the wounds were opened.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he suffers thus with great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	And many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And one arrow was stuck in the body of the king's son who had fallen from his horse, and he was slightly leaning to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	And the arrow was completely lodged.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was summoned to the physician after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought her out with great subtlety, and did not find her;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he could feel a prickling and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it might be the point of the arrow, I put up his left shoulder blade and stomach lining, because he was swelling.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I found the arrows of the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the ointment to my hands every day, and healed the wound directly, and so kept the patient for a long time, until he felt the arrow was inside his nose.
et il le me dist.	and it told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I placed above the wound a medicinal mixture of acid and corrosive by hand every day, until it had dried up, and I tried it, and felt that the head of the arrow was drying in the place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I closed up the opening of the wound with that acid mixture, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and after four months had passed well, I saw if the wound could be closed by cutting open my flesh to both sides of it, and it would not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Now cease not from subtilizing and devising of means, until I took one day the tongs well made, according to what their form will come in the end of this chapter, as long as I do it, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restore it then, and the wounds were soldered, and the patients were completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I have told you the quality of extracting arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, because books cannot learn everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But wise masters have done little beyond a small thing, and on what is present but failing, they find new work and nine instruments, by the discovery of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of limbs where they are stuck, except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or because they enter from the left or otherwise.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps over because it enters is an arrow entering into the inner limbs, and now it never happens again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if she does not jump anymore, then let it remain as long as the inner limbs are putrid and infected, and let the issue come out.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if she is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it remain so for some days, and move with every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then she jumps, and if she does not jump, if there is a puncture in every part of the forehead, until the inner limbs are enlarged, and then take it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if an arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and it waits until just before one of the veins of the brain, and some of the accidents that I mentioned are revealed to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	but if it is not treated promptly, but let it stay there for some time, because if the arrow comes to the same spot as an abscess, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone and does not come out right, and it stays there for some days without a serious accident, then the ingenuity of handling the situation.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply stuck in such a way and cannot come out without great effort, if you administer tartarium inside, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the patient until they are fully recovered.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is put back in the body of man if we cannot see it, if it has filled the entire cavity.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then if there is no suitable instrument available;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot cut through the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow wound, and there is no bone or nerve exposed, then try to cut as long as the wound will allow.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are nails in the arrow with which it clings to your ear, if one of two parts is stuck in the flesh that you can reach, then break or bend the nails so that you can pull the arrow.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And carefully, so as not to break the arrow, pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, even if the pain persists until the wound has closed, then treat it, for the extraction is an agony.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the blood causes a counteraction, then follow what we have said about the treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And beware of the incision on the nerve and vein, and put in place as you wish to move the arrow quickly, or soon or firmly.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And put the patient according to the shape he is in when cutting into the arrow wound, because this is the greatest aid that can be, and if you cannot do it, then put him according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow wound that comes from the other side, or if it is blocked with something, or if the skin is inflamed in that place which can be seen or felt afterwards:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cutting down therefore on it, as long as the tongs can take hold, and then pulling out;
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it is stuck now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand around it, until it enters into the bone, and widens the bone, then pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, so let it go again, and then continue extracting until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if an arrow is stuck in the wound, pour out the entire arrow.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the arrow comes out, and you see pouring medicine, then pour the medicinal instrument into the wound so that the points of the arrow enter the hair of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then pour out, and if the arrow is stuck in the hair, then pour the medicinal instrument with points entering into it, to help extract.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched down, it is best to copy the whole shaft to where the venom is or is supposed to be, if possible, then treat the wound as it seems.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow sticks out or pierces or to the belly or bladder or chest, and it is near a vein, then you can cover up, if you must.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and protect the vein and nerve, and then pull them out, and then cut the wound, because it is necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is cured.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used to treat arrows is like a bird's beak, and thus it looks:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form that has hair on the end is like a bird's feather, to press against the tip of the arrow, just as it is:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the pliers for pressing and packing if it is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of veins from which one can cure oneself are thirty-one, because there is an opening for sixteen (this means that)
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	two branches which are after the ears, called "the two 'herbs'.
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two armpits of the two eyes, called "aspire".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein which is swollen at the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the head of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two guidebones which are on the collarbone;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins which are in the upper lips of the mouth, and these are called "augerich" or veins.
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins below the tongue;
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	the veins of which one is commonly found in each arm,
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cerebral vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the head" among the people.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the moine is called "faste", and it is composed of the cerebral and basilic, and they call it the people of the village "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilic is located at the right side of the shoulder, and they call it the people of the village "vein of the stomach", and it is above the flesh, and it is that from which one heals, who manifestsly opens up above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the radial vein is the one that is between the auricular and the ulnar vein.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg, where it is at the foot are three veins.
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is beneath the wing of the pocket on the left side of the shoulder, and the second one is at the ankle on the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nesse", is located at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein that is located behind the ears if aided by ancient remedies for catarrhs and migraine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the vein, just as I tell you, and is that by raising the patient's head, and stroking the cloth or veins with a rough fabric;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then the patient's neck is tightened with a strap, until the two veins are visible behind the ears at two levels of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	because then one must press down on it, and where you feel the pulse beneath your thumb.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Take the lancet, and the braid down through the vein just beneath the bone; then lift your hand up to the entire vein head, and strike and cut and let the vein go well. II must now penetrate into the wound as far as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then tighten it up so that it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The sickness of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if there is old inflammation and soreness, and accustomed ophthalmia, and at the place of the tears drops into the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the sicker are as I said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and thus the patient must tie his neck so tightly that both veins appear open.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and they feel pain beneath their throat and then let go.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the vein up high towards your throat index finger, and pull out the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up high again, and strike it, just as you did in two other veins, and do bleed according to your necessity.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then put the patient down, and place your index finger on the vein for an hour, then cover with cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then tie it off, and let it be until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and this is what we have discussed and treated in their application and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The sickness of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the sickness of the head with ancient diseases such as emigration and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that patients who strain their neck in twisting will be aware.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "surgical saw", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press upwards from your hand, or from another thing, and let the wound bleed according to how much you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then deliver to the patient the neck, and tie the vein so that it is clean and there is no bleeding whatsoever.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	All things considered, it is not necessary to make them too big.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And the strong one goes awry, for the bone is near, and by chance, breaks the sharp thing when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The injury of the two veins that are in two arteries if you hold fast to the eyes, and to the sinew, and to the redness, and to the swelling in the ear, and of the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the qualities of their injury are such that the patient is straining his neck by twisting any ligament, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the wound, and if there is a strong wound through it, a little long with a sharp flame, a little wide, for there is no chance of being caught.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame (cautery) is subtle, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then do a stitch in the wound, so much as you have need, and then tie it up tightly, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The affliction of the gallbladder with bile, so much as it causes fever and soreness, and diseases of the face, such as emigration and redness that comes upon the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and if the patient contracts an ulcer so much as his collarbone is contracted, then strain his nose to your left hand, and take out the subtle flame, and strike it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in that place, and he will begin to bleed now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not cut too deeply, and make a clean cut according to your necessity, then bind it for one night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The disease of the two joints often leads to tightening of the sinew, and at its beginning, it brings on ulceration, and much sickness, and boils, and corrosions, and itching, and ulcers, and lesions.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the disease are that if the patient strains his neck away from one and both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and if the master is standing over the patient's head and the patient pricks the vein in a long way just below it, then treats the wound seasonably, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then remake it again in the other vein, then cut off the ligature, and tie on the veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it stay just until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	About the disease of the liver.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sick of the veins of the lips help themselves to coal in the mouth, and to the corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and do not heal.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And if the wound has been healing, then sit down in front of him, and tie his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the hand, and look at both veins, one of which is in the right palm and the other in the left, recognizing them by their black color, and also because there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	so that both of them are cut, and if you do not recognize one or the other, and you are in doubt, then cut the larger one from each part, and just like this for all four veins, since it is a same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the sickness in the lower regions of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The diseased veins that are below the tongue aid after the head is cut open, and it is at the constriction of the neck, and with illnesses of the eye, and with illnesses of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and if the patient is skilled enough that he sees the disease take place between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks under each corner at a vein black;
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Healers then both should be called, and do not go too deep in, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the throat which we commonly heal are healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they are pricked with a sharp millet seed, or an olive seed subtle like needles, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are long and subtle according to the size and narrowing of veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of flame mint is very famous and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary to open the vein cheeks that contain flat blood with large visible wounds, and that contain large wounds and trouble.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of a flame olive.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And is more subtle and pointed, and it is for healing the small veins subtly, or there are subtle clots like citrus.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilica stain, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are in the throat, and around the neck, and on the chest, and in the stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is suitable for the lord that he applies the application, and that he warms himself from the artery that is under.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and fresh blood comes out, then it is considered to apply stitches, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and let him not prick at the flame, but cut it off as one does with a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the gallbladder is not opening visibly, it is advisable to remove it and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want only some of it, or you heal the vein with the same medicine in the arm.
elle apert manifestement;	it opens visibly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cuts at the flame with a needle, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the skin on the vein, it is also advisable to remove the arm, until you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the vein of the entrails, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a needle.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And beware that you do not strike the artery when you see the swollen limb, for it is of the artery:
eschui la donques.	Choose then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see swelling above as in the urine of a child, and there are no redness or subtlety, know that it is not of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry up then, and put on your surgical knife lengthwise, then cut open the vein if it is not inflamed, for this happens often;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	if his arm sticks, and leaves it so, and does not move the limb.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let there be fear, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if it is not bound by bandages and he swells up, and you wait for him, and the medicine is not present to him, then strike the artery as soon as it opens, because the head of the joint will retract.
et estainche li sans.	And if he becomes bound by bandages.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a scrape from the fistula, and cut it, and take one of the halves and tie it well onto the other half.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if he is not bound by bandages, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if it is not so, then he must cure him as we have said, with the powders that bind wounds.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the bindings do not cause more harm on those who are subject to small wounds and the swelling of the joint in the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The afflicted vein in the middle is relieved so that it treats wounds of the head above, and wounds below the body, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is fitting for the master that he warms himself in the vein below, and if he cuts too deeply, and he injures the nerve, and it swells, and the wounds become infected, and by chance he cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve is often opened many times, and if it does not open in any man for its subtlety, it is fitting to sanitize the instrument afterwards.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and spare the nerve from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it with length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The afflicted cerebral vein is relieved, so that it treats wounds of the head, and relieves the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is prudent to heal by pressing on the flame of olive oil or the flame of myrtle, for this is the most safe of all veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	But it is wise to seek the lighter route first, and do not grieve about it if you must try it for the first time, and start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance they swell in some men, but you should not grieve about it the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know is that healing comes only if it serves to preserve health, and to ward off diseases from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the healing be done in one of the three veins that are or cost:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	It's a type of head cold, fever, basil.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it is prudent to be cautious at the beginning of prayers in June, and in autumn and winter after fasting, when the signs of replenishment appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must be cautious on the first day or third day after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The cure which is administered for various diseases has no fixed time determined, but it is taken when needed at any hour or in all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not advisable to cure children just before the age of XIII or women who are pregnant only up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	It does not suit to heal those who have passed LX years (60 years).
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wishes to be cured by whatever means, it is advisable that he should take a light purgative enema if he has much phlegm retained, so that the veins may carry away the superfluities of pus which are harmful to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	No one will recover if they are too spoiled by meat, or who is drunk, until they become such.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if war has weakened the person after colic, vomiting, and decrease of belly wind, and frequenting woman, traveling, watching, and journeying, and that which weakens all the body, either by something of the arm or through the flesh;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly remove the humors, without excess, by meat and drinks and medicines, if you have one such poison.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then take a bath, if no thing is forbidden, in order to remove the wound, and you will recover from the pain of the vein on the third day, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep that day of work free from toil, pain, and luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be careful and cautious, and let the healthy ones be given precedence over those who are sick, and rub the arm two times or three, then pull out the bandage halfway, because when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot correct itself without.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the affected area with your hands, until the veins swell and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then anoint the healthy ones with a small amount of heated oil, then place your left hand on that vein below the affected area, just enough to stop the blood from flowing and prevent injury.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that are as empty as strings to the seller, and so are those that are full of windiness, so that when one puts flame upon it, it retreats to flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is like these;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the vein opens up, then it is because the wound is too narrow, for this reason they must be advised on these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens up the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	but if not, then it must be repeated again on the spot or above that point, as soon as possible, unless it inflames.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the wound is inflamed and the patient hopes for it, if they let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	By chance I will come across abscesses.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter the bath, then resume treatment if it pleases;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small or if it has no subtle treatment, and you doubt that it will not spill much blood as you see, then trust in the same wound itself directly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and if it happens quickly, so that the flesh is inflamed;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	because this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh inflamed, do not resume treatment again, and put a little of lard on it, because it lightens the body with pain, and is soft in this liver that the lard.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus serve the ligament of oil in each wound to heal the veins, so as to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and thus makes a triangle and bowstring from it, when placed on the limb;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if so subtly applied as to be without splinter or when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess that has happened many times, namely when the vein is only open at those times or the opening of the vein is small, then you hasten and place on the limb a moist sponge soaked in water and in wool, and restrain it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of the vein's blood, and if it remains on the limb for some days without any inflammation or greenish color, then it will not be harmful;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see it, put on no powder of aloes or myrrh made from camphor, monstrous thing, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times, an abscess and appearance occur in the cavity of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put then your hand on it, and if you find the left joint swollen under the pressure of the hand, so is that appearance bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Avoid then that you do not put on any of that which we have said, for in some cases without cutting the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but apply a plaster of plaster to dry the joint, then heal with another treatment, until it is safe.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And deal with each according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is not black, let it be left out for as long as it turns red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see a large wound, let him so it is subtle.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too swollen, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	It is best for one who is thin and weak, and needs extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and apply more ointment.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is best to make him sick less often, and he must be made healthier by cutting across, not pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	This method of healing is safe from bleeding and clotting of nerves, and it's better than the long healing of a small wound or the short healing of a large one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose fever must be treated with healing, it is best to give them warm milk in the juice of green apples.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	In case of a high fever, apply to the pulse three times or four; if it is of cold complexion, apply a poultice made with warm milk in honey syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, canel, ginger, and cloves, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If the patient has a wound on his palm, after a great amount of bleeding, it is advisable that he drink a broth of char and a subtle-smelling syrup, and use other things as we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If he is to cut off one arm and heal it again, if this is allowed, when the patient is weakened by great bleeding, it heals little by little, according to the continued power of the virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If he who is to cut off one arm after the first bleeding has strong flesh, it heals in seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the eleventh hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever is to be healed in another part, if it must be healed the next day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For it has much blood within the body which is causing a high fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to apply a large quantity and enlarge the wound so that it fills with blood.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you must reward all the healing conditions and put your hand above some fingers so that death does not come through the wound, for this often happens when a nurse is careless.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see someone releasing their arm, and making the wound bleed again, and if the limb is lost then it must be closed by pressing on the place.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	but if it's bent, then extend the arm immediately, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it stay as long as it heals again;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or point at the tip of the flame, until the vein that was cut has stopped bleeding and you place a poultice made from silk soaked in water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is sprouted, so let it be and do not strangle it any more, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to treat the wound a second time, then in the same vein as before, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healed in place of the vein on the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the treatment is that the patient puts their hand in hot water, until the pulse is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Now let my be linked moderately, so that the vein appears well, then let it be healed now through and through, neither too small nor too large.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the large ones be cut and let it be healed well near the joint of the hand, so that without any issue, if you put the hand in warm water, and let the wound seep into the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's in the suppurating state, do not put the hand back in warm water again, because you will make it worse by putting it there.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the health of this vein is more saved from all other veins, than there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The health of the little finger of the right hand is worth more than all other diseases of the liver, and it is this way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and pour it into hot water, until the vein is cleansed, if you see.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it turns to blood, and if you cut it the whole length, so that nothing hurts.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not cut too deeply, for the nerves are now exposed and have no covering, and then put the hand back in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and will not come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound as much as necessary, then put oil and sinew on the vein to solder it hastily, and do this for each place.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness of the sinew in the left hand is worth the disease of the mouse, and do this just as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spine is worth as much as all other diseases that are in the body, since they are such as those of the mare's, and retention of flowers, and disease of the rains, and of the joints and the legs old, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And cleanse the wound if it is bleeding, and that the patient puts some powder in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it stops, and binds above the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is at the ankle and goes up quite far on top of the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Let the inflammation rise then or if it becomes more swollen at the knee, what does it do?
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you cut on the flesh above the bone, guard well the nails that are beneath, and cut the wound to cross like cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let it be still in its place.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out by itself, he puts the foot in the water, and lets well empty the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the salve is needed for the first time, if it recurs a second time above a little spot, because the liver is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do it similarly with the sponge of the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The liver of the saddle vein is in the heel of the foot and its wound is worth the pain of the groin, when it is cut.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And if the quality of its salve is such that it enters a vein, and strangles above the knee four times by twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if she opens, so the healthy one in all kinds of ways that you can do it, and through crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and copy its muscles because the limb is swollen, and it is very tight in all directions.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, the healthy one will burst through anywhere near an opening or under a foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the fingers;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make as much cut at the vein that you see, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and bind it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wind sickness
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	ventooses are made of horns, or of nails, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and evacuation is done in two manners:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by pricking and attracting blood, or by pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this evacuation which is done by pricking also has two manners:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is to all fire, or to fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and evacuation made by pricking and the extraction of blood is done in twelve leagues of the body, so that one may be entirely without flesh on the head.
