et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are covered with the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two more on each side of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and those beneath the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the winded of the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the wound above the groin;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the wounds in both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the wounds in both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the wounds on both heels;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and wounds from the stings of small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason they do not become inflamed, unless as is done with venous bleeding;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that they be drained, unless by fire or the heat of the senses, in no disease that comes from overfilling, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity of illness calls for it, or due to custom, then bring each one an hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to venesection, have heavy heads;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and to those who experience repletion and redness in their face, and head, and neck, and darkening of the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and to those who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and are bleeding.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and to those who are dreaming, and seeing blood and nausea and death-like things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is in its third month, we command to be ventilated after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sick of the moisture so much hurts the ear ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not good if only this happens after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this ventilation is in place of the head pain, and it is not good for those who have a cold complexion, or who have diarrhea, because it causes great harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore, it is not good for the old man to use it, or those who have head cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become blind, and for this reason they must put the ventilation instrument a little further down by the doubt of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation on the neck is in place of the head pain and the gallbladder, and because of this, it brings tightness to the breast, tearing of the channel of the stomach, and thirst, and bloating.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is considered necessary to give more space, because if she holds too tightly, so the bowels become obstructed or the stomach and liver.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The swelling of the lungs when it cost on both sides of the chest causes severe head pain, eyelid swelling and migraine, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is a sign of the sickness of the basilisk;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is necessary that you command the lord to press his hand on it when it comes, so he does not cut the artery, and does not be present during the bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The swelling under the chin if it is severe causes illness of the mouth, and corrosion of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in place of the wounds on both sides.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are worth the disease that comes from heat and overcharging.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The lacerations of the cutes (groin area) are valued as much as three veins on the arm, because they cause blood loss from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the master to not cut too deeply, for the flesh is thin and he knows beneath (the surface) nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The abscess on the buttock is valued in terms of the hemorrhoids at its foundation, and with diseases (diseases) beneath, it is fitting that the abscess be large and filled with mucus, so as to have need of being properly treated;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and in case it is subtle, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and if I do great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	When the swellings on the legs heal completely, because they attract blood from all the body, and are relieved of old pains in the joints, and the inflammation, and the swelling of the bladder, and they bring down the flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are replaced by the two kneecaps, and the two calf bones, because they weaken the body after long use, and make it come to a more severe condition.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the swelling is that you put it in first empty, and then as soon as possible, and place it quickly, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see the new redness and inflammation of the wound.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then make it hot, and apply dressings, and take precautions in the arrangement of the bodies, because there are those who have turned to charcoal, and some can bear it better.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if you must cut only once, and if you must make large wounds, and deep ones.
et suce legierement.	and suck more gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if they are not very large, then you must cut twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to open the way of the great blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	and if they are very thick, then you must cut a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we wish to treat the little blood drops one by one, if we suffer from a single cut.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then let's continue frequently;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the clot is thick, then cut into it with great force, and when you reach the edge, it's clear that the wounds will be perceived suddenly, and treat those who have thick skin and hard; and who have pores that are easily open, that you anoint them with oil, ventouses ( probably "sponges" or something like a poultice, but I don't know what "ventouses" is supposed to mean), and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it's in the violet oil, or in sweet almond oil, or in cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it's in yew oil, or in cassia oil, or chamomile oil, or anything similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the flow is large and cold, you must take turmeric oil, or balm oil, or anet oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If those whom you have healed with a tender touch and large pores, do not put any oil on them, but rather wash them after the application of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain melon water, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, so they lift themselves from the air, or from water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great swellings rise from the old wine, or from fresh water, or from decoctions of anise or camomile, or other similar remedies.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and they should not be cured with suction in front of the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and they should not sleep after the suction, and it is necessary to make them warry when they are to be suctioned and when they are swollen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware those who are sick with colic, and if they are not too swollen and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if they should take cold things, such as apples, grapes, and lettuce at ease, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and let them eat children, and broth of chestnut, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, should drink syrup of honey, and sweet-smelling wine in moderation, eat little, and eat children's flesh, and small birds' meat, and pease.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he will be vented, should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is convenient to give some food such as tripe or mutton at some houses before the venting, or after, to comfort the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and they should be taken in small amounts, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The ventouses that are applied to cause pain are those placed on the liver, and on the mice, and podagra, and on the stomach, and the bowels, and the joints, and the groin, because these members do not bear to be pierced, unless it is done for a painful symptom in one member, if as we apply the poultice to the breasts when they heal.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	Because of the viscosity that is at the member, as we put ventouses on the belly and on the mouth to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and cut off the pain, when there is inflammation or stone, so that by its attractive power at random the inflammation goes away, or the stone falls out of place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and so it is done when one places him on the liver and on the gallbladder when there is retained viscosity, and these venthouses are empty only to suck out;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes only with cold water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in such manner that one fills the ventouse with hot water or with it has cooked herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction to be administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And the surgeon takes two fingers of breadth and half a palm deep from top to bottom, and puts one on the costal region toward the middle of an inch, so that he can push a needle in, like placing an arrow, and it should be soft so as not to bleed the patient when putting on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and it has an inch of a crossbar of iron or wood to put a bandage on, and there are large and small ones, as needed for the sickness and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the ventouse wounds in children are different from those in old people, and in thin ones than in fat ones;
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And you must then put this ventouse on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	wrap the bandage of wax or linen around the limb and put it inside the ventouse through the crossbar so that the light will be at the bottom of the ventouse, so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and place your thumb above the gap where we have said so, so that when you want to pull, if it goes in vapor, and take out the vacuum;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and bind it along the same line as before, and rebind often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the vacuum, which is used for treating diseases of the pleurisy, is given to all that are inflamed, with no thumb or gap, and is applied only when it is filled with inflammation, and placed on the member alone;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	No dressings are applied except in the limbs where one cannot put a vacuum due to smallness, like lips and gums, and similar things;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And when you clean out the chest with charcoal, as two or neither, and similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the patient are such that when you find ulcers in waters that are sweet and free from poison, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them in sweet water until they are recognizable and have nothing in their intestines;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then wash with vinegar and antiseptic, then rub the affected area until it is red, and put on ulcers;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are flat and have healed, if it can be done to put a tourniquet, do it, because this is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the limb high, and then put it in water, much better, and then warm it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the limbs are healthy too soon after the operation, then put on a linen cloth soaked in cold water, and put it on him, until his breathing is stopped.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if his breathing is multiplied, then put on a solution of crushed glass, or vinegar, and similar things, until he stops breathing.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or apply to him moist flesh peeled of snow, and let it sit on the limb until it dries up, if it will stop now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you have more of this matter, take other openings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the openings do not want to take place, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until they occur, and then put them on, and immediately when you feel the opening, let it dry.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they bleed, so sprinkle some powder on a little distance and with the broken thread or ash, they will now stop bleeding.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of fractures begins.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, young book, that the leeches from this chapter have never been seen by any of the ancient books, nor do they read any letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason is strange the knowledge in our land, because I have never found a good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except by the knowledge of ancient books, for which I have studied so much and treated the science, and through experiment, and from my accustomed life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained here and condensed it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that must be brought, as I did in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we speak in this prologue of the book about the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and keeps it on the virtuous, so that those who have experienced this art noble learn and acquire it, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break or dislocation or torsion or any other occurs to anyone, it is fitting to hasten and heal the patient from one part and from another, if no remedy applies, as weak of body, or sick, or old;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if their joints are too stiff, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and if they apply cold remedies, which are cold poultices, and charon of bird and of celery, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not stuff themselves too much with viands that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about a hot abscess or swelling of the member;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to their former good governance, which they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore themselves, it is fitting that you nourish the patient with foods that cause great swelling, such as those which have a lot of viscosity, like bread cooked in water, and risotto, and testicles, and pork fat, and oysters, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because the swelling causes more sprains and sooner the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of old and aged do not heal well again nor can they be soldered according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, neither those which are too tender, just as the bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, if you apply the broken bone to a large tendon that holds together and joins the limb in one piece, until it heals as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not to its full strength, and for this reason they must be nourished with large foods, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And finds that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all sorts of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that grow inward, and others that grow outward, just like the thickness of a hairpin to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with just a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each method has its own instrument and proper equipment for the restoration, according to what is remembered in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that bone fractures are recognized by the fact that the limb is twisted and open badly due to lack of use, and it feels painful on the presser of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no tortuosity or lump at the joint, and the patient feels no great pain, if there is not even a break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have some degree of tortuosity, or a small crack.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move your hand, but apply medicines that come after this, and then restrain now with subtlety.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And knows that the break that occurs in the arm, and are the two parts of the joint, he must now put them on an equal basis, so that the abscesses do not come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the cauls come, he must leave one day, until the abscesses are laid to rest;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then he puts him on the muscle where you can easily and carefully fix it, and knows that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those in which there are pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if you separate them into two parts, whether it's between the hands or fingers, or on the palm of the hand, or at the wrist, or one cord and on the hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are reduced, you reattach by all means possible in their proper place, and avoid that through your work the patient comes to have an additional injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and put the two bones together in the best forms possible.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And he feels well with his hand if you think he is not feeling well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If the dressing is made well, and he is not strained too much, nor pressed so as they who do this work make his blood hot and contraction to the member, just as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is set to right, instruct the patient well that he does not move, nor watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And take care that the limb is so fixed that he does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in its proper place, and therefore you should put him into this certain condition that he does not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And keep him straight so he is set correctly, lest twisted movements occur when it is restored again;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb will be as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Things which the member is broken are various in size and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers.
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is convenient to wrap bandages of linen soft and subtle;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those which are large, such as thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is convenient to wrap with a strong and thick rope, for the large ropes embrace the entire limb, and tighten it equally in all parts, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind with light straps, three turns or four according to the limb, and tighten with one hand all around the rope, then go up to the break and tighten it less than the break so that the break will soon move a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the joint little by little, until you press a great part of the healthy limb, then take another ligament, and turn it inward toward the broken limb.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the lower part of the break, and hold it firmly but not too hard or too soft, as we have said before;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put linen rags or bandages between the ligatures until they are all even, then tie everything with an upper band, and then put your well-made stitches on top, if there is an abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if it has inflammation or an abscess, put on soothing ointment to the affected area, and what removes the inflammation, let it stay for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Pursue a tight grasp upon your joints, and let them be of the size of a wide cane resounding, or of wood from which pliers are made, or palm tree shavings, and let them conform to this form:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is fitting that the joint placed on the break be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and so large as it should be, for the length of the small or great limb;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tie the joints in such manner as you did on the first incision, then tie above with an arrow-shaped thread, as you did on the first incision over the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the narrower it is, the worse.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is fitting that the thread be fine, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For the big nails, as I have seen in works of fools who make their clothes with twisted threads of linen, and it is a great error, because the nail can not be even if it is too subtle, and it should not be more than two fingers' breadth between each nail.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is wounded by arrows after an injury, then tie off those places with linen or woolen strips so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a break and the joints are fractured, I will say this treatment after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to tighten the arrows on all members, even the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to put nails forward less than five days or seven, or more according to your safety after the incision that follows.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and thus here is the way of ancient embalmers to restore breaks, dislocations, and twisting.
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and thus you take flour that remains on the walls of the mill, and mix it with a great amount of water, and put this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, into use, for it is the common way of the embalmers to restore breaks in many situations, and especially in women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plastering restores the break and the dislocation and the twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take a mixture of resin, linseed oil, and gum arabic and apply it to an area X.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Glass and aloes, applied to area V.
alechil VIIII З.;	Alechil (likely a type of plant) for the seventh day.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make powder from flaxseed and mix it with honey.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the complexion of the humours is hot, apply this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, but at the risk of many deaths.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster that is valuable for twisting.
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take care of and examine; for the child is Z.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mercury and aloes, for seven times nine.
acaice VI З.;	Asa six.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Onice Arabic ten Z., and brews well, and confits with water or honey, and administers.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to splint is when you use sticks and set the bones straight, and ease the following pain, and cut with the bone, and fracture.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Apply linen cloth, and poultice of mold in oil cooked, and put on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not heal, but they are good for soothing abscesses and properly placing bones, the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to splint that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Burn the leaves of dried figs and earth leaves, and crush them together, and make paste.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat a plaster for the healing of a bone fracture and to relieve swelling from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of violets, chamomile, flowers of violetts, wheat flour, from each one a part.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	And crush it and mix with wine, and apply to the limbs that are heated; or mix with moist coriander water, or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to treat is stronger than the first, when an abscess comes back to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take root of violets, and sesame seed, balsamum, meletemne, and without succa, and flowers of violets and chamomile from each one a part.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And crush it and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iporas writes in his book that you should not put broken bone on the limb to restore it, rather, one should use a mixture of cerote made from wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between too hard and too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that one must place the broken limb on high in order to restore, using dry things moistened with hot stuffs, such as myrrh and aloes and incense, just like we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of treating an abscess is worth its pain and suffering:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mutton or horse flesh, or nails of birds, and vermilion, and cut them evenly, and pound them, and make it into an ointment, and apply to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then lay the wound open a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, or has his bones in their proper place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not lay it open by skilled hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the wound, or it pricks, with rest or swells, then hurry and lay it open, and apply the ointment now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a lighter cloth, and a sponge moistened with seawater, and plunge into the water, and lift up the wound until the itching ceases, and the pain is alleviated;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Instruct the patient to leave the limb rest for an hour, then place it under a dry cloth, moistened in water or oil rose, and tie it up with a bandage until you are sure of the wound's size.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And let the inflammation rest on the limb, and try to remove the pain, then resume gentle cutting, a little emplastre, and do not strain it too hard as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and very gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess swells and is red and painful and inflamed, I have already treated it by draining and stitching, just like I did before when the pain came on.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if the limb does not come to anything of what we have said, do not untie it unless after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and at no time let it stay for 20 days, as one sees, until the fracture is set, and approaches the healing of the bone above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	And therefore you must restrain it more than once, and swell the meat around it, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the liver drying more than it should, know that it will not come to pass.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then it arises from a hot cold fever, every time you dissect, and this be the case for all alike, one day after another.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	therefore cut the nerves in the limb, and immediately stop what is done by the foolish surgeon, lest they return the limb twisted.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	this is bad, and if it's due to fear, and I see no other thing but that one should loosen and straighten it directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	From diverse ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are predetermined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	there are fractures that are caused by the blow of a sword, and the collarbone ossifies all the bone below the fractured surface, just as it is compressed or shattered.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason it is called a "haicheure" fracture.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	when the sword strikes the bone from underneath in order to pierce it, and this is called an "absolute" fracture.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and there are two kinds of wounds for these fractures, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact into a hollow space, or tearing, or fracture of the bones by stone, or through the bone on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has an open fracture which is near to the bone under the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	and if the wound is closed in the bone as subtly as we cut hair, and there is a small split, then this fracture is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	If the wound is made or by hitting with a stone, or by falling, or by some similar thing, and it causes a piece of bone to fall into the wound, and the hairs are as they were when the cauterist was firing the cauldron over the cauldrons;
si entre li piere dedens.	If a stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have moist bones under their head, like children's skulls;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and occurs in all such fractures where small pieces are separated like stones.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak on his behalf.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all kinds of fractures by the removal from them, and the inquiry has been tried, and by the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of the hair is known by this: that when one discovers the bone and strokes on top of it, if the fracture opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be careful for all accidents in the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, paleness, fever, eyes turning red and swollen, and other similar signs, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no extraordinary accident and you expect a good outcome, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the sickness comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is fitting to take out the bone before the fourteenth day at night when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	But if it is in this state, then hastening to take out the bone before the seventh day, will only make the skin below the bone corrupted, and accidents that we have described will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture comes just to the skin covering the brain, then you must break the fractured part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And take the head of the sick person, and cut open on the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound as well as you can, because if there is a discharge of blood, it comes when uncovering the bone or abscess; and as much as possible aid with what is needed, and fill the hole with moist cloths in oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and make sure there is no discharge of blood.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two different ways.
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is that you copy the narrow cutting before, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then after this treatment, a more severe amputation is performed than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have many kinds of knives, some are thin and others are wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And when you cut lightly, so that you do not hit the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and thick, it is necessary that you pierce through it, so that with knives you administer them carefully, not piercing too deep, lest the blade go beyond the bone into the flesh, and should have a margin or a circle around the point, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is necessary to have many of them, so that each one comes into its own place at the spine of the bone, so that you should have knives for every part.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three kinds of trephines:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	Those that pierce through the broken bone should place one trephine on the bone and turn to both sides until you see that the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the trephine on another part after a little while, and do this all around, then make cuts in the bone's space between the perforations, and do it more subtly than you can, gently, just like we said, until you pull the bone to your hand or one of the instruments you have, such as pliers, pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the skull.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and made cuts, if there is something left on the bone that remains from another instrument similar to an incision, but it is necessary that it be more delicate and subtle than those other incisions.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it does not heal after a few days of small bones or scales, if the bone is lightly damaged in the joint.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with stitches and bandages as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And other ways of work are those that the Galenians say are more accurate;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and this is their strong word, and it is their saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary to uncover a part of the bone, in that place where the break opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you put under the head of this incision a lens-like shape, because it is this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut it from one side, and if the affected part is two sides, so that the cutting is against the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then use a small hammer above, so that you strike the bone lightly all around, and be well guarded with the cloth underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	She should be burned at the bone, very lightly, because feeling the pain well, and fearing.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone is not pierced through the cloth until now and only the top part of it is struck so that small pieces form, then cover with the roughness again and remove the scales at the razor-thin sharpener which you must have in various amounts to provide for each person what seems most convenient according to their work and figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have before many rough razors, and after subtler ones, and do not cease to do this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other types of hair cuts and subtle breaks, it is necessary to apply care according to its nature;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that has no answer for him who put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, it is necessary to pour oil of roses on it according to its quantity, and moisten it with linen cloth;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three and moisten it with wine and oil of roses, and put it on the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do what is easier than you can, so that you don't strain the liver, then serve it again under another link, and do not stretch it further except when the wound heals by itself;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it remain like that on the first or second day, until the swollen part is alleviated, then remove it, and administer medicines such as wild garlic, flour of bees, powder of incense, and herbs, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make a powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and administer medicines to heal by bleeding.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and make sure the wound is thoroughly cleaned, so that you don't leave any discharge, and don't leave it with a bow (a protective covering), for when the bow comes together over the scalp cloth, it can cause blood to run and bring great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when you put above something sharp, he will pierce through.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful whether they will doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if it does not come from the fire that we have placed on it, so that its virtue has effect, you must press a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in vinegar made into a cloth, and put it on the sharp thing.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of this kind should be done to him, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that the two bones above are never broken, or one alone, for they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, so it is fitting that you poke your little finger or puncture into the wound, and put equal that break inside your thumb, and in a pouch as needed, until the blood returns according to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone and it cannot be returned to its place, so that you put a small peg into the head of a nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is of two parts, so do it again, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is appeased, then poke with a needle into the wound, and cover the head with linen drapes, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	When you put something else in its place, if it is broken.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the tents be so thick that they fill in the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And doctors said that you should moisten the swellings in butter, and move each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to be the best thing to me, but it is advisable that they are moist in the making of auburn and powder of flour;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then let the tent stay until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never put in or nose plugs made of goose fat in its place, and if the wound is deep and wrapped tight, and it holds the dislocation, and blows into the patient.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	if you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	If the abscessed joint comes near while you are working, then put some cold or moist cloth in oil or rosewater, or apply a poultice of dung.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if there is no abscess, then apply plaster by omission, made from flour of suture, and powder of incense, mixed with wine vinegar, and put on light spoons, and do not bind the nails.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the nail is small, and it is fractured into small pieces, then take out the splinters that are convenient to do so, and sew the wound, and apply plasters and ointments that are suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it has no wound within the nail, then treat the nail, and apply poultices of onion, until he is cured.
de la routure de la mandibule	About the fracture of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is fractured without any open wound, and there is only a bruise inside, without breakage in two, but only a slight separation of the cheekbone, if one weighs lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is fitting, if the fracture is in the right hand, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the patient;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	In case of the broken jaw on the left side, put your right thumb into the break and gently push it inside, and press with the other hand without force, and tie an even knot.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is displaced in two parts, it is necessary to manage the extension of two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	If the movement of the teeth happens or a fracture occurs, where there's a strain from a thread of gold or silver or silk, then apply to the broken jaw a layer of ceramic and a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on the double cloth an even-sized big nail well-made or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it above where you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the swelling changes, and he lays on it for three days, then puts it back to what is changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And apply plaster on it, with powder from the mill, mixed with a lot of water or flour of sement, after you have cut out the wound;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and apply a lighter layer of plaster, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, let him remain until he is cured;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times they are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If an abscess comes to a head, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	and if it has a fracture and a wound together, remove as much of the bone as is exposed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if the removal of the bone is subtle and conveys no dangerous consequences.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have removed all these bone pieces, and it does not stay in place, apply the wound dressing, if it is large, and put on suitable poultices according to that, in order to heal the wound.
de la forcele	of the fistula.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fractured bone is forced further multiple times in the shoulder region, and the fracture occurs according to three kinds:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	When it is broken and split in two, and has pieces, and is lighter to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	when there is a break with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the injuries are when the break is with an injury, that you have two ministers, one of whom will hold the arm because of the bruised break;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then puts equal the break on both, so that the form becomes as it should be, and there is no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have to extend further, then put under the shoulder of the patient a rounded spear of cloth, or linen, and so thick as your necessity requires;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and let it heal, and strain the bowstring to your hand, so that you tie the break in equal parts, as is fitting.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot treat the head of the pain in front because it comes from within, so that the patient lies on his back, and put a pillow under the shoulder, and pour the medicine down the throat, until the bones of the pain are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then direct the break to your two sides, and if you find a suitable splint, tie it up as much as possible;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and bring the lighter pieces together, and if the bone cannot be joined in any way, then cut at one of the joints you have made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but so that you put on beneath this instrument a safeguard to protect it;
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not made of wood, and be as long as you need, according to the size of the bone and the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And if two heads are broken, so that you see them, and one is large and the other is narrow, as is the way of the wound that you have made when treating the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of a bone being broken, if the wound cuts, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt that the bone is broken, then apply the wound with strips and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms on your flesh, then apply rose oil, asbestos, and vinegar to it, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The straining of the bone, when it is near to wounds and swelling, is that you place on the bone powdered flour from the mill, and aloe ash, and put lightweight cloths over it, and put a spear underneath, if you have need.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very thick bandage of palm leaf width, and put one double drap over it, and the poultice;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin needle of three inches long and broad, and pass it through the bend of the bone, so that the head of the bone is still there.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the needle on the fracture, and turn the bend of the bone up towards the neck, and below the healthy part, and below the diseased part;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and tie off from each part, and when you see that the ligament is holding the fracture in place, and you see clearly that the needle does not move over the fractured bone, then repeatedly reward it each day, and when the ligaments are tightened, restrain them;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the broken place, to lift the joint upwards;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If the arm is made to heal by stretching the shoulder, or you tie the arms to the neck, and do not untie yourself in case of a bad accident, it will be sound after twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then resume the plaster, if you see that it needs it, bind it and leave it in that way until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it will be restored by the thirty-eighth day, and less than a few men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	But it often happens that the shoulder breaks or is twisted in some way, and does not heal unless through its own movement.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	so arrange the limb according to its own shape and form, and reset it in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put powder of the mill on the wound with a large amount of oil, and light blows, and place above it an adhesive bandage.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then puts on a large and subtle needle, slightly larger than the shoulder, and sews under the skin of the shoulder in any part, so that the needle cuts evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then tightens it to a great band firmly, so that the needle does not move from its place, and examines the stitch every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it is applied, so tighten the band, and place the needle as if it were in its proper place, and put the patient on their chest.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is restored in twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is fulfilled, release the dislocation, and be sure, for it's not that the bone will move lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if one piece of bone is pushed forward and does not adhere to the wound below, then raise it up, and the bone, and do as we have said in soothing an abscess with great heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The flesh is broken at no time in its middle, but it happens occasionally;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often without warning.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, so that it inclines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of feeling, and swelling, and sometimes vomiting blood, and in order to open up the marrow in the broken bone, and the sensation is much worse.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that when the patient rises from his bed on both sides, and he puts this cloth between his shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the two breastbones with your hands, and skillfully places equal between all the ways you can, until the figure of the bone becomes as it should.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then puts over the joints and the fragments of bone on a subtle layer of salt, or of another lighter material, and wraps it up in one piece, and ties it to the bone so that it doesn't move;
