et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And turn the round link to the back, and bind it immediately, and reward each hour the limb, and if she relaxes, then bind.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	But if he wishes to release it, because of corrosion or itching that comes on the limb, or pain or abscess, if one hastens, and releases it, and scrapes away the pus, and addresses those who have come from various treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then scrapes away the pus, and binds it so that he becomes whole.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the fracture of the ribs comes only after a large amount is taken away from the back, and towards the head inside, because they are brittle.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and this feeling is good for an investigation as should be.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are such that you must put the fracture back, as it seems fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and tie with a splint, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the break of the ribs is slanted inward, he feels the patient great pain and point, just like from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the cloth;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and he is filled with pain and pus, and swollen and vomiting great plant of blood, and it is from bad health, and the old men have put great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who claim it is suitable to administer foods that swell the belly in order to push the fracture into its place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless an abscess has come from a burnt flesh.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then cut it out.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And said none of us that you should put vinegar on the flesh, because it will cause wounds, and it is like reason;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	but doubt remains that the vinegar will not attract the exudates to the flesh because of the weakness of its constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that one must cover the limb with a moist linen in hot oil, and place tentes ( probably a type of bandage) between the ribs to make the wound even, then treat with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot suffer from the bone which pierces the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is fitting to split open the ribbed part of the broken costal, and it is fitting to put certain instruments to ward off the wound.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must pierce the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and heal with poultices, until it is cured.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess comes to a head, put moist cloths in olive oil on it, and apply heat.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until the abscess is gone from the area where it occurs, and if there are ulcers on the surface of the wound or wherever it must be cut into, until it is cured.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Never occurs a fracture of the collarbone and there has been no collapse.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens that he cannot tell if he will be sane or not, take care and see if you notice these signs: when his hands are soft and swollen and lifeless, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you poke them with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortal in these other dispositions, and if he is mute and feels well when you restrain and press him, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will recover, if you put them on treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you see whether it will heal or not, take care if the vertebrae are softened, and if the wound is in hands, and on the back there may be a great falling out, and an emptying with a violent want.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when one has soiled it under his belly, he vomits without voluntary will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he becomes aware of it on his back and tries to relieve himself, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that they are fatal.
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	unless it is treated with special care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if such an accident does not happen to him, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that if there is an abscess hot, you put oil of roses or oil of mustard seed on it, until it becomes calm.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then puts on one of the plasters comfortable and drying, and ties it with a bandage, and instructs the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and does not lie on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if some bone has been broken, it is advisable to cover the wound;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then take out the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if they are large, with a seam, then apply the dressing and tighten bandages tightly, until it is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone of the bone is broken, which we call "chiese of la kowe", then pour some wine from your left hand into a pouch, and place it equal to the other hand on your palm, then apply plaster and stake above, if you have need.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then tie it up, and if it has bone exposed, make it above, and the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the femur
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It rarely happens that the bone of the hindleg is broken, and if it has, then there would not have been for a little bit of relief to the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and let it grow long, and draw back to the paraders, and comes to the patient pain in the shoulder, and joint, and swells what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And if you are restored to health, then stretch out your hand above, until you reach the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and sees which is the break and the form of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the break is only in the head, then straighten that broken limb, until it has returned to its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or declines inward, so that it points to the inside, have the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have straightened it, then apply plaster, and put on a splint of wood or horn, and bind the break so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply the plaster under the ribs, until the limb is straightened.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	If an abscess comes to a head it must be touched gently until the abscess is allayed, and apply what we have said previously.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	And then return to restoration, and bind as necessary, if there is no further injury.
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The joint is that which is between the sleeve and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of the two manners:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	whose one is that you take a flat piece of bone, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And hold both joints in place with two ties, and set them above the patient on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Now the joint is broken in the shoulder, so let it lie still until it comes to an assembly, and take out a piece of bone from the shoulder, then put upon any weighty thing or let the minister extend it below.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then put the splints in the breakage equal to its joints, so that the breakage returns when it is suitable.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that you must put the patient above his head, and tie his neck, then command to two ministers who one holds the thing that is on the breakage in their hands, and the other holds below all the ligature, and each of them extends it to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then tie the ligature below the breakage, and above the breakage, and extend each of the ministers to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the breakage is close to the head of the shoulder, so it is fitting that you put one linen under the assembly, and the other towards the joint, under the breakage;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and if the breakage is towards the joint, so it is fitting to put one linen lightly, with ease, until the breakage becomes even on its place and on its joint;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	the fire cautery instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if the abscesses come, do not strain them again for seven days, and put on a linen bandage soaked in oil rose, until the abscesses are eased.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then strap it, and the way to strap it so that you put plaster on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the side.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the bandage on, and strap it onto the shoulder, and onto the arm, so that the arm is in its place, if no other thing prevents it, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use stakes, and place one larger and stronger stake on each break, and set them apart by two spaces, and so that each stake is as large as it can pass through the break at three points of each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then pull out the stakes, in the same way as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, stronger and less constricting.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the position of the stakes and the constriction, just as we have said, in the place where you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess there, leave it tied for seven days, just as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then look at each one of them three days after the tie, to see if it prurites or swells up, and there is no discharge in the limb, or a pus forms that cannot come out because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is true, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents happen to him, then do not free his limbs until after three days or more, and the patient should lie on his back, and have his hands above his stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	And place this cushion under the injured arm so that it is smooth and even, and watch each hour of the day or night whether the figure of the broken limb moves, or if the ties are loosened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it appears by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat which we have placed in front of you, in such a manner that the meat is at room temperature.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to regain his appetite, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the arm and the leg are to be put back in place after forty days of treatment.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then so he must be untied and given a bath and administered medicine for the wound to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is tight and swollen, so it stays tied for three days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "scapula", one small and that is where the pocket.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and that is under, towards the small shoulder;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Sometimes it breaks only the large scapula or only the small one, and sometimes both join together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small scapulas are broken, restoration is light and healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large scapulas are broken, healing is poor, and more grievous than when both are fractured together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small fossicle that is broken alone, then it must be extended lightly and put back in place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it's a large swelling, then they must strain it more strongly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch it out to the extent of its swelling, and pull up the pouch of his hand higher than others, and lower his fingers more below those of others, so that he crosses himself on him himself, and stretches out above it even more, so that the patient suffers no pain at all;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then stretch the minister's other arm to the part below his hand, or near his joint, and another minister on the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put him on equal ground, in his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no matching piece that can be held close to the joint, and you cannot restore it to its proper place, then fix it with bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if it's with a break and an injury, I have spoken to the singular surgeon;
si pren la cure.	so take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration, a piece of flesh falls away from bone, then apply to it a plaster made of cerote, oil rose, and white wax so that it is neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And let the surgeon take care of it gently from above, so that the abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then take the bone and apply plaster made from powder of wheat flour mixed with a great deal of water; put the splint on it, so that the splinter of the fracture is straighter and slightly more forward than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and he knows that he must have six splints or an increased number of arrangements:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	or if the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and bind more tightly above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less when applying it, as I said at the beginning of this chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and that the dressings above the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or harsh;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let it be the children, from which it is strained, of linen, neither too fine nor too coarse, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is suitable to raise the limb in cold water until the itching is soothed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be tightly pressed down to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the tightening, and if the joint is loosened and the bone is separated, and it seems like a similar thing, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the numbness persists and cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then it is fitting that you loosen it a little, and let it stay like this for some days, until the numbness goes away, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if any of these things do not happen to the patient, so that they are freed after twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	until, then put the hands on his neck, and so that his necks are even, and guard against movement and trembling, and sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the composition and the constitution of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand break
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand there is a small amount of breakage, and it comes but pain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the finger of the hand is broken or bent, it is wise for the patient to tie a cross on it, and sit straight in front of it equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then places his hand on the broken joint, and stretches out the limbs of the broken bones, and sets them even and square until they are well set;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and applies plaster and bandages, if there is no abscess, then he puts in a stake according to the quantity of the wound;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and should be wrapped with an i-draped linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the tendons near the belly of the finger, he makes a bandage-stick, and instructs the patient to tie it around his broken finger;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then strain of a long thread, and if the limb is bound tightly as big as the thumb of the hand, and the binding, just like it should.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the breakage is in the fingers, it is advisable to place an arrow above and another below on the foot, so that the fingers are covered and straightened; then tie all around the hand, and bind the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	and if the fracture comes to any of us, then that is bound tightly, if it is done well so as to be equal, just like it should.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and the binding with the palm, and if you see that it binds a small pin straight to lift the fracture, and does not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is on other joints, just like it is in the index or one of the others, so that it is done well and he binds with the healthy joint which is after.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them all at once in a single tie, what value is it, or you put on a pin, just like if they were bound.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And be wary in the restoration and arrangement of an abscessed place, and heal those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	The part of the bone breaks.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the collarbone is often broken, and one can see it when they turn in front and behind.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And the restoration is done by linking the above to the broken bone, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patients lie on their face, then stretch out each of these limbs equally.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and it is when the bone is mended into place.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the joint of the bone, then it's one of the bands to the point of the finger, and the others below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is proximate to the groin, and then there should be the ligaments of the groin, and the extension below.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	The patient should put the mirror on the equal bone to its two hands, so that it is according to his natural figure; and then apply plaster, and tie, so that the abscess does not come again.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if it has an abscess on the same place, let him allow it to be soothed and then return to its original state and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary to wrap above the break with a bandage that is twice or three times wrapped around, and then let the swelling stay for a while, then turn the leg so that the toes reach the root of the nail, and tie a long thread between the thigh and leg, under the knee, and tie the calf tight with a thread from below, and wrap the top with thread.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn on the knee and on the thigh the bandage, then put a bandage on the bruised place, and put an arrow on the bone of the knee;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then apply the knee bandage eight times between the thigh and the fold of soft cloth to secure equal tension, then begin to tie a bow figure III or IV on the bruised place;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the more you pull up on the bruised place, and less the bandage will be tight.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then hold both two joints of the thread that you have tied between the knee and thigh, then tie three more arrows above, before going back down to the head of the thread until you reach the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and if it does not move from its place, then leave it as is, because there will be no abscess or swelling or other similar signs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if this happens, if it dislocates, and addresses itself as we said before, just as we have explained many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that hold it, then you must fix them, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if you cannot, then it is necessary to break the limb and treat it.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and the treatment as we have said, until he becomes healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And there is no time when the cartilage is broken as we have inserted needles, just like in the shoulder and arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	because all the restorations done will not close the wounds of the patients.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And the bone is restored in three days, or a little less or more, according to the diversity of the complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the femoral channel
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	The body of a child has no fracture, but it often bends.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, but is only a crack or split, and has pain to the wound and the flesh, and it hurts very.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is done as we put equal what was rough on its surface, until they are assembled what can be.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Now put the plaster on it, and put a round stake in it, if you need to, and bind it as it should be, then reward all the arrangements that we have said about other breaks, just like an abscess is hot and another similar thing.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you put it on each individual case that he thinks so, until they are healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Knowing that in the leg there are two bones, so one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it happens that all other breakages are as when it comes to the arm, and for this reason is the restoration like the same arm, and the work is all in one. And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg of every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, so turn it before.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, it feels great pain, and he sees it well;
et torne desoz.	and turns around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	And therefore straighten the extension, and put it equal, and tie the strings equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but it is necessary that the broken piece be small and lighter than the extension;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and align it according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed all your work, take two strips of cloth that are red and purple which stain the leg from one side to the other, and be long enough from the knee down to the bottom;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap in two strips of cloth one on top and one on bottom, and tie them in the middle so that the leg cannot incline to the right or left, and thus it is good;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And none of them have taken care to treat the long swelling of the leg, and if it has burst open, and they put the leg in a binding garment to prevent movement, and doing this properly is done in the break where it has injured.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And move each person every day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	So that the patient becomes sane.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone fracture of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not come to a break, but sometimes the bone of the foot breaks and sometimes it is bruised, and there is no force required except for shock at other dislocations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if he has a broken bone in his foot, and you see the bones protruding one over the other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he were walking, and then place your own foot upon his, so that the bones are raised, and press hard until they realign themselves in their proper place.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Instruct the patient to apply plaster and bandages on that area; and place on the lower belly of the foot a small plate with two holes for the fingers, then bind the foot at the ankle, then when you have wrapped the strips around, and other things necessary.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if you release the bandage, because you will find that the bones are even, whether they are broken, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if they are any broken bones that need to be reset, just like we said the bones of the hand.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then put the broken bone in a splint according to the length of the two bones, and make it slightly larger; then bind with the foot that plate I mentioned earlier.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, put one splint on each bone according to its size, wrapped in the first strip of linen, and bind with that plate over the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and when standing on the top of the head of the table so that his belly is exposed under the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	and it is also necessary to remember all the other things I have said about other fractures.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each case as it may seem appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of a bone at the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the woman’s bones are broken, so that she becomes enlarged, then incline her to the part of her back, and hold her behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the wound with the nature of the patient’s cloth, and put also a large amount as in the stitch.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then bind the woman, and lift her back little by little, and then sew the cotton until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and brings its bone with the stitch.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to pee, so loosen the cotton, and when she has peed, put it back again, and do this seven days or more:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If the break is restored, and you see, take a vessel of wool, and tie it to the puncture with a string, and pour all the vessel into nature:
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow through the string that forms, until the vessel is sucked inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	nature will restore the break;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be filled with cotton, and let it so for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone at the shoulder joint of a man or woman is broken, or the bone of the hare, restore it in the same way as we have said about the bone of the hare:
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and are not hidden from those who apply their study and use, and they heed my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fractures mean more suffering in the right path of restoration:
enten le donques.	and therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the vagina, when it is fractured, take an owl's beak and insert it into the vagina.
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then wrap linen bands around, and let it remain for three days or more, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of breaks with wounds.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a break with a wound, especially if it's great, so that the bone of the shoulder or arm joint, or similar, is set now, if what we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the wound is clean, then apply the vinegar again, if you have nothing else, then restart the healing process in that same hour or the following day, unless an abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes, then wait until the next day to restart the healing process, up until the abscess is calmed down, and do not touch it again on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the broken bone appears near the joint discovered, it is to be put at a gentle point on your fingers, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the splint is not provided for placing equal to your hands, since this instrument made of iron with seven or eight fingers, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is a master's work that must be done by three or four, as needed in each type of fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be small and thin enough, so that when compressed against the limb at its location, it does not bend;
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And is called "palanche", because the curved metal is placed on top of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and after one turn, so that they are even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	But if the break is subtle and the splints cannot grasp the bone properly, it is advisable to copy the skull bone, so that the splints have hold of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	But if you cannot put the bone back in its place, as we have said, then make the cut with an instrument suitable for it, whether sharp or dull.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	Then take what is remaining in the bone, of sharpness and of small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that he is not in his natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	So that it is in its place, then make a hole in the tied rope in vinegar black and proper, as this is what it should be.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	And do not put any cream or other thing on the wound with oil, lest it bring rot and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	Then administer ointments as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all over, according to the quantity of the wound, and be sure well that the wound is not bound with the break.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And many times have these fools done this, and brought the patient to death or corruption at least once;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And let the strainings be more gentle and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that more accidents will happen as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, do not put up with this, instead.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap it tightly, in place of the splint, with hard bandages and tie.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after the first day or second day that the bow has healed to the wound, so know what you have put on top of it all wine, and apply the ointment healing wounds, just as ointment of four parts and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is fitting that you dislocate the limb a second time every day, morning and evening, until it is softened and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limbs be dressed in a certain way so that the bow heals along the leg more lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the wound opens again every day and it cannot heal but falls apart bow, see how small pieces of bone there are, for that's why you should cover the wound with a poultice, and remove all those pieces which cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If an abscess comes to the leg or in another manner of corruption, then it is fitting that you cure it, according to what he advises in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	But if the bone is broken and protrudes through the limb, as it does with the arm or shoulder, and other large limbs, do not treat it yourself, for many times one dies, but allow it to heal by itself.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	by chance you will die after twenty or thirty days from the wound, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then let her go.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of wounds that come on from a boil.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	we come many times after the health of the fracture, especially when it's near the joint, and behold what a thing to see is the form of the limb.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance may not be able to do the limbs their natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Be cautious therefore if it is fresh.
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if he administers medicinal drugs such as aloes, incense, and mirrors, and saffron, and myrrh, and similar things, insofar as you have none of these things, or all together, and confound them with a mixture of vinegar or wine, or oil.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put it on the nose in poultices, and strain well, and do not loosen it with your hands for a day.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	And then dislocate again, and repeat it so often until the knots are removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you strain on a flat bone that is well done;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	because the property of the flat bone is that it removes all swellings over the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot is turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, so that the wound above, and the apparent superficiality.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you return to it without rasp, until it is removed, and the cure until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb that is weak after childbirth.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the bone break is restored and stays after the weak and subtle limbs, if it happens for many reasons;
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	For why one is so bound, because he was too tightly tied, and not so tightly bound as it should be.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because he had too many ties, and the swollen part cannot come to the member.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or for too many swellings;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too great movements, neither in its hour.
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is to make the patient eat less and make his body soft, until there are multiplied in him.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer a bath, and do to the patient joy and amusement;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Then put powder on the limb, so that the powder attracts the great swelling, and the joint rises frequently from the painful water, until the swelling subsides.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One de la main after the health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is ugly all over, then do not try to restore its natural shape.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if you do not believe the foolish people who say that one must break a limb all new every time, and many fools have done this in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this kind of work is blamed, and great harm comes, and by chance one dies.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	If the nodulations and tortures are fresh, then it is advisable to let them arise from hot water, or to cook herbs like violets, roots, and malloloth, as if they were of wormwood, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	And make the flesh softening like aqua fortis, as it is done, and take the wormwood mucilage, and confection with honey or sesame oil, and make it soft again;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or take grease figs, and grind them with wheat flour, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no joint is straightened by constant and prolonged friction with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And make the joint move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortuousness is hardened and hardened, like stones, and needs treatment with hot oil, if you choose to apply it to the bone, at the subtle incision.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put a bandage and study the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs for no apparent reason, if you think now is the time to restore it properly.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	But if delayed, the swelling increases, and by chance it is put back in place at pains.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because one should not move the swollen part until it subsides:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times brought on inflammation and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	whenever it happens, if you treat the patient to make him whole, then set him free, until the swelling subsides.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then warm the affected limb with hot water and oil, then reset it lightly, and treat each member as its own treatment comes to pass.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of the treatment for dislocation of the shoulder joint, since it is a painful injury.
des mandibules	of the jawbones.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Sometimes the jawbones are dislocated and outwardly, and the dislocations of both jaws occur in two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	They are a little bone of their own, and soften a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated, and hang down to the elbow, and cut the saliva from his mouth so he cannot hold it, nor close his mouth, and with speech is overcome by his tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it recurs more often in various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and finished, then you must reset it quickly, and do not wait.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in this manner that the ministers hold his head back, and pour a small quantity of the mixture from one of his hands into the root of the dislocated jawbone within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other hand be covered, for it should equal.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And put the mirror on him equal, so he regains his place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	But if the jaw returns swollen, especially when both jaws are affected, apply warm water and oil until it softens lightly.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not force it to return to its normal state, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned to their normal state, and the mouth of the patient is swollen slightly while softening, apply moist cloths soaked in rose oil made from melted oil and beeswax, then bind it lightly with lint.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, with their heads between two pillows, so that he does not move either to the right or to the left, and do not force anything else, but rather give him gentle meat until the pains are gone, and the jaws are numb.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then take what he wants lightly, and do not work on opening his mouth to mend and drink, until the jawbone is well closed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset to their point in one hour, and are not converted back to their places, then fever and sickness are set in, and by chance, belly pain occurs, and by chance, vomiting of clear blood.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	and when you see this, then know that it's deception;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many have died from this in seven days.
de la forcelle	of the forearm.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forearm cannot move across the bone inside the joint and against the flesh, and it is dislocated every time without fail, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the limb against the palm of your hand, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the joint that is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	He will not recover, and if he is dislocated at all, so that it is reset to its proper place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then applies the plaster and bandage, and ties it, instructing the patient to rest until they are healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and so again is brought back the head of the spine, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	About the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Which know that the shoulder joint is dislocated in three kinds:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	because it dislocates at the lower end of the humerus below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the joint of the elbow;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and sometimes dislocates above, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	And do not let it dislocate behind the shoulder, and do not let it dislocate within the chest area.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And dislocations often occur below the collarbone, especially in those who have little strength, because they are suddenly exhausted.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	But for those who have enough strength, the pain is intense and it goes to unbearable levels, and then they become unbearable.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some people that they are struck or crushed, and an abscess forms on the shoulder hot with inflammation, and they think they have a dislocation.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore, one should examine it carefully, until you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	And then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And this is known about dislocations when they occur below the collarbone, and you will find a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will discover differences in their diversity.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find a hollow at the shoulder, and beneath the shoulder there is an asselle, also like the one we have seen;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot return his hand to its normal place, nor can he move it in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also if she is dislocated above, and it's not hidden, because you will find it clearly at the shoulder.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this kind of dislocation is not very serious to treat when it's new, or if the patient is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the minister lifts the hand of the patient up high, then puts his fingers beneath the asselle, and lifts the joint to strength in the normal place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And let the minister relieve the hand, and extend it upwards, because he puts it below;
si venra hastanment.	if it is to be cut.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said before in our hands each day, then it is fitting that the patient be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and he gives him an arsenic and fenugreek and meliloton concoction in water, just as is given;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then let the patient be placed upon his back, and put an assel on his shoulder with a linen cloth that is not too soft nor too hard; then place your finger on the joint of the talon, and lift the head of the shoulder very gently, and treat the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	And other servants take your head from the patient, so that it does not move again.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	That shoulder returns to its place now, and if you see it move according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that there be a person standing in the room who is greater than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and standing on the opposite side of the patient's back, and tapping his shoulder below the incision, and lifting the incision upwards so that the patient hangs from the arm;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And another servant treats the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then they must put with them any heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And again, one returns in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And let it be so that you pull the long bone into the earth, where the joint is also in its proper place, as if it were being pushed, and not too big or too small.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	and then it is placed below the patient, but if he has a soft covering above, and the patient lies on the long wooden staff;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	and then his hand is stretched out below the other side of the joint, and the joint returns to its place as soon as possible;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a long bone of two forearms and four thick ones, which have their head right in front to enter into the hollow of the femur, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then tie up on top of the head with a cloth so that the flesh does not bleed, then put under the bone of the sick person;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and take one arm out over the length of the bone, and tie the assistant to the bone, and the arm on top of the shoulder, then put the arm over the pin of an eschele with a wide diameter, and stretch out both hands below, and let the body hang down from another part;
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint is put back now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, in any manner whatsoever, it is suitable that you put below the abscess a spear of wool equal, then place the plaster made from pumice powder on it with incense and onions of oil, over the entire shoulder and around, then strain from beneath the abscess immediately, and turn the bandage back onto the plaster, and encircle the hand around its neck, so that the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	and it is fitting that he should not move at all, until the limbs are comfortable, for he will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move more after five days or seven, and move him.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and it cannot be softened, then it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen from moisture or from some other reason, then it is advisable to apply cauterization at three punctures, as he is placed in front of or beside the cautery container.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do this and after seven days it becomes loose again and the joint will not hold, and he cannot lift either arm above, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder have been struck or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint is never put back in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that occurs near the elbow and knees or at the back, is done by impulse and stretching of hands, and it requires another joint.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure until he is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes pain in the member, and slow movement, then use the patient baths many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder cut
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the shoulder joint that becomes dislocated at a point, and again returns to its place.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	And it has come loose from all parts, and itself at front and back, and the dislocation is not corrected, for one sees well and feels well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And it loosens according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased limb with the healthy one, so the wound can be seen clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, or reach one's shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is fitting that you also reset it so that the abscess comes to a head, because if the abscess comes to a head, then it will be painful to put it back.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	And perhaps it cannot be reset entirely, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	and if so, it's better than other dislocations, and is accompanied by greater pain, and perhaps death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And restoration is done, when it's such that you can put her back together again, then extend your two hands to hold her.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And let the arms be spread out, and the hands straighten according to the cost of the forearm, desor and desoz, and push the joint onto its place, or at the root of his palm, until it comes back to its proper position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation, so that it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and very strong on the root of the palm where the finger is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not return to its proper place, apply strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and let the two men extend the arm, and straighten the elbow with both hands, so it does not move at the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm on each side, after having wrapped a double cloth, long and wide.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the fingers grip the joint at his hand, if he cannot apply oil to soften the joint, then push the joint together until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when she is at rest, if you put on plaster with egg white, and stretch the strain, and bend the arm towards the shoulder of the patient, and leave it for some days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, release the ligament and leave it.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint does not hold well, renew the plaster and ligament, and leave it for some days, until it is firmly fixed.
puis le deslie.	Then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels great pain after the return of the joint, and it is quiet, then bathe him and rub him well, and press until it be soothed.
